12 min
The Purpose of Confinement in Rahn: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Distinction between Hanafi and Shafi'i on the purpose of confinement in rahn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on permanent retention (ḥabs dā'im) in rahn and distinguish it from the Shafi'i view, and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to determine the pawner's right to reclaim the pawn.

Core Idea
Hanafi: pawn is confined for collection (yad al-istīfā') → permanent retention; Shafi'i: pawn is confined for sale → no permanent retention.

This lesson explores the foundational difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the legal nature of rahn (pawn). While both agree the pawn is held as security, they differ on the purpose of that confinement. Understanding this core disagreement unlocks many subsidiary rulings, including whether the pawner can demand the return of the pawn before debt payment.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Recall that the Hanafi school views the pawn as confined (maḥbūs) for the debt, establishing a 'hand of collection' (yad al-istīfā'). This grants the mortgagee a right of permanent retention (ḥabs dā'im) until the debt is paid.
The pawn is not owned by the mortgagee; only possessed for collection.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the debt is attached to the object itself (ta'alluq al-dayn bi al-'ayn), and the mortgagee's right is to have it sold, not to retain it permanently.
Thus, the Shafi'i view does not recognize a right of permanent retention.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i basis: rahn is a contract of security where the object is designated for sale to satisfy the debt. Therefore, the confinement is only to facilitate sale, not to give ongoing possession.
This leads to the conclusion that the pawner may reclaim the pawn if alternative security is provided.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school argues that if the pawner could retake the pawn, the mortgagee's right of collection would be defeated, contradicting the purpose of rahn as a security that requires continuous possession.
The mortgagee's 'hand of collection' is meaningless if the pawn can be removed at will.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafi – the pawner cannot demand return of the pawn before debt payment, even with alternative security. Shafi'i – the pawner can demand return if he provides adequate alternative security, because the purpose (sale) is still achievable.
This difference appears in many subsidiary issues (furū') enumerated in Kifāyat al-Muntahā.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالحاصل ان عندنا حكم الرهن صيرورة الرهن محتبسا بدينه باثبات يد الاستيفاء عليه وعنده تعلق الدين بالعين استيفاء منه عينا بالبيع ويخرج على هذين الاصلين عدة من المسائل المختلف فيها بيننا وبينه عددناها في كفاية المنتهى جملة
ترجمہ پس حاصل یہ ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک رہن کا حکم رہن کا محبوس ہونا ہے مرتبہن کے قرض کے بدلے میں یہ استیفاء کو ثابت کرنے کے ساتھ رہن کے اوپر اور شافعی کے نزدیک دین کا تعلق ہے عین کے ساتھ وصولیابی کی غرض سے اس سے عین کو بیع کے ذریعہ اور ان دونوں اصلوں پر بہت سے ان مسائل کی تخریج ہوئی ہے جن میں ہمارے اور ان کے درمیان اختلاف ہے ان تمام کو ہم نے کفایتہ المنتہی میں شمار کرایا ہے۔
تشریح ہمارے نزدیک رہن کا حکم یہ ہے کہ رہن دین کے بدلہ میں محبوس ہے تا کہ مرتہن رہن کے ذریعہ اپنا قرض وصول کر سکے اس لئے کہ مرتہن کو ید استیفاء حاصل ہونا چاہیے یعنی وصولیابی کا قبضہ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک دین کا تعلق مین رہن کے ساتھ ہے نہ کہ اس کی مالیت کے ساتھ اور وہ صورت فقط بیع کی صورت ہے پھر اس اصل کلی پر بہت سے مسائل مختلفہ متفرع ہوتے ہیں جن کے بارے میں مصنف نے فرمایا ہے کہ ان تمام مسائل کو ہم نے کفایتہ المنتہی میں بیان کیا ہے پھر یہاں بھی مصنف نے ایک جزئیہ پیش فرمایا ہے کہ ہماری اصل کے مطابق چونکہ تا ادا جو دین مرتہن کو جبس دائم کا حق ہے لہذا اگر راہن رہن کو واپس لینا چاہتا ہے تو اس کو اس کا حق نہ ہو گا ورنہ اس سے موجب رہن جس دائم کا فوات و فقدان لازم آئیگا۔ اور امام شافعی کی اصل کے مطابق راہن کو واپس لینے سے منع نہیں کیا جائے گا کیونکہ واپس لینے سے موجب رہن یعنی بیچ کے لئے تعین میں کچھ خلل واقع نہ ہوگا۔ مصنف فرماتے ہیں اور بہت کی جزئیات و فروعات ہیں جو اصلین مذکورین پر متفرع ہیں جو مسائل کے درمیان میں آپ کے سامنے آتے رہیں گے۔
So the conclusion is that according to us, the ruling of rahn is that the pawn becomes confined for his debt by establishing the hand of collection upon it; according to him (Shafi'i), the debt is attached to the object, collecting from it by sale. And upon these two principles, many disputed issues are derived, which we have enumerated in Kifāyat al-Muntahā. Translation: So the conclusion is that according to us, the ruling of rahn is that the pawn is confined for the mortgagee's debt by establishing the hand of collection upon it. And according to Shafi'i, the debt is attached to the object for the purpose of collection from the object itself through sale. And upon these two principles, many issues in dispute between us and him are derived; we have enumerated them all in Kifāyat al-Muntahā. Commentary: According to us, the ruling of rahn is that the pawn is confined for the debt so that the mortgagee can collect his debt through the pawn, because the mortgagee must have the hand of collection, i.e., possession for collection. And according to Imam Shafi'i, the debt is attached to the object itself, not to its value, and that is only in the case of sale. Then upon this general principle, many different issues are branched. The author said that he has stated all these issues in Kifāyat al-Muntahā. Then here too, the author presents one particular: according to our principle, since the mortgagee has a right of permanent retention (ḥabs dā'im) for the debt, if the pawner wants to take back the pawn, he will not have that right, otherwise the purpose of rahn, which is permanent retention, would be lost. And according to Imam Shafi'i's principle, the pawner will not be prevented from taking back the pawn, because taking it back does not disrupt the purpose of rahn, i.e., the determination for sale. The author says that there are many particulars and branches that are derived from the two mentioned principles, which will continue to come before you among the issues.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage summarizes the core difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the legal nature of rahn. The Hanafi position: the pawn is confined (maḥbūs) for the debt, which gives the mortgagee a 'hand of collection' (yad al-istīfā'). This means the mortgagee has the right to keep the pawn until the debt is paid, and if the former wishes to reclaim it, he cannot force its return. This is because the mortgagee has a right of permanent retention (ḥabs dā'im). The Shafi'i position: the debt is attached to the object itself; the mortgagee's right is to have the object sold to satisfy the debt. Consequently, the Shafi'i school does not grant the mortgagee a right to permanently retain the pawn; the pawner may reclaim it if he can provide alternative security. Upon these two principles, many subsidiary issues (furū') differ. The author refers to his work Kifāyat al-Muntahā where he listed them all. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilāf) is illustrated: if the pawner wants to take back the pawn, Hanafi says he cannot because it would defeat the purpose of rahn (permanent retention); Shafi'i says he can because the purpose (sale) is not affected.

Key Terms
محبوس (maḥbūs): Confined/detained: the pawn is held by the mortgagee until debt payment.
حابس دائم (ḥabs dā'im): Permanent retention: the mortgagee's right to keep the pawn until the debt is fully paid.
كفاية المنتهى (Kifāyat al-Muntahā): A work by the author listing disputed issues on rahn.

D) He may take it back only with the mortgagee's permission

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school grants the mortgagee a right of permanent retention of the pawn until the debt is paid, based on the principle of yad al-istifa; the Shafi'i school limits retention to the purpose of sale, leading to different rulings on reclaimability.

The Condition of Dayn Mazmūn for Valid Rahn
Condition for validity of rahn: it must be for a guaranteed debt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition that rahn is valid only for a guaranteed (mazmūn) debt and apply it to differentiate between existing obligations and future promises.

Core Idea
Rahn requires an existing, obligatory debt – collection (istīfā') follows obligation (wujūb).

In Hanafi fiqh, the contract of rahn (pawn) secures a debt, but not any debt qualifies. This lesson examines a key condition: the debt must be mazmūn – guaranteed and already obligatory. The reasoning from al-Qudūrī's matn shows that the purpose of rahn is to enable the mortgagee to collect the debt, which is only possible after the debt is due.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states that rahn is valid only for a dayn mazmūn. Determine what this means for validity.
2
Define dayn mazmūn
A mazmūn debt is obligatory (wājib) and guaranteed – typically an existing liability like a loan already given, not a future or conditional promise.
Key term: 'mazmūn' implies the debt is due and collectable.
3
Understand the ta'līl (reasoning)
The legal effect of rahn is to give the mortgagee a hand of collection (yad al-istīfā'). Collection can only happen after the debt is obligatory (wujūb).
4
Apply the condition
Test whether a given debt qualifies: if the debt is already obligatory (e.g., loan given), rahn is valid; if not yet obligatory (e.g., promise of future loan), rahn is invalid.
The mortgagee's right to collect must exist at the time of the contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا يصح الرهن الا بدین مضمون لان حكمه ثبوت يد الاستيفاء والاستيفاء يتلو الوجوب
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور رہن صحیح نہ ہوگا مگر دین مضمون کے بدلہ میں اس لئے کہ اس کا حکم ید استیفاء کا ثبوت ہے اور وصولیابی وجوب کے پیچھے آتی ہے۔
تشریح رہن صرف دین ہی کے بدلہ میں صحیح ہوتا ہے کیونکہ رہن کا حکم یہ ہے کہ مرتہن کو رہن پر ایسا قبضہ حاصل ہو جائے جس سے وہ اپنا قرض وصول کر سکے اور وصول جب کر سکے گا جب پہلے سے وجوب دین ثابت ہو چکا ہو۔
He (al-Qudūrī) said: And rahn is not valid except for a guaranteed debt (dayn mazmūn), because its ruling is the establishment of the hand of collection, and collection follows obligation. Translation: Al-Qudūrī said: And rahn is not valid except for a guaranteed debt, because its ruling is the establishment of the hand of collection, and collection follows obligation. Commentary: Rahn is only valid for a debt, because the ruling of rahn is that the mortgagee obtains such possession of the pawn through which he can collect his debt, and he can collect only when the obligation of the debt has already been established.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn of al-Qudūrī. It states a fundamental condition: rahn (pawn) is only valid for a dayn mazmūn – a debt that is guaranteed and obligatory. The reasoning: the legal effect (ḥukm) of rahn is to establish the hand of collection (yad al-istīfā') for the mortgagee. Collection can only occur after the debt has become obligatory (wājib). Therefore, a future debt or a contingent debt not yet obligatory is not suitable for rahn. For example, a loan already given is an obligatory debt; a promise to give a loan is not. Thus, rahn must be for an existing liability.

Key Terms
دین مضمون (dayn mazmūn): A debt that is guaranteed and its obligation is established; typically an existing liability.
وجوب (wujūb): Obligation: the legal quality that makes the debt due and payable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because collection (istīfā') can only occur after obligation (wujūb)
C) Because the debt is not yet a tangible thing
D) Because the mortgagee does not have possession

Key Takeaway
Rahn is valid only for a debt that is already obligatory (dayn mazmūn); the mortgagee's right to collect from the pawn depends on the debt being due.

The Hanafi vs Shafi'i Nature of Rahn
Explains fundamental difference between Hanafi and Shafi'i on rahn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the fundamental difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the nature of rahn and identify the thamarah al-khilaf regarding the mortgagor's right to reclaim the collateral.

Core Idea
Hanafi: rahn is detention for recovery; Shafi'i: debt attaches to collateral for sale.

This passage reveals a foundational dispute: does rahn (pawn) detain the collateral for the creditor's right of recovery, or does the debt attach to the collateral itself, enabling its sale? The Hanafi school, emphasizing yad al-istifa (right of recovery), treats rahn as permanent detention. The Shafi'i school, focusing on ta'alluq al-dayn bi al-'ayn (attachment of debt to the collateral), treats it as a temporary means of sale. This difference branches into many detailed rulings, particularly on whether the mortgagor can reclaim the collateral before repayment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two foundational principles
Locate the Hanafi principle: the collateral becomes detained (mahbus) and the mortgagee gets the right of recovery (yad al-istifa). Locate the Shafi'i principle: the debt attaches to the collateral itself to enable its sale.
These two views are the roots of all subsequent differences.
2
Understand the Hanafi position
Rahn means the collateral is literally detained for the debt. The mortgagee cannot use it, but holds it exclusively for recovery. This detention is permanent until the debt is paid.
Permanent detention prevents the mortgagor from reclaiming.
3
Understand the Shafi'i position
The debt is tied to the collateral itself, not just to the person. The collateral can be sold to recover the debt. The mortgagee's right is not to detain but to have the collateral available for sale if default occurs.
Attachment does not require permanent possession.
4
Trace the thamarah al-khilaf
If the mortgagor wants the collateral back before repaying, the Hanafi view prevents it (to maintain detention), while the Shafi'i view permits it (sale is unaffected by possession).
This is the key practical consequence mentioned in the passage.
5
Recognize the branching of issues
The author notes that many other derived issues follow from these two principles, which he enumerates in Kifayat al-Muntaha.
This dispute affects multiple chapters of muamalat.

And upon these two principles many differing issues branch, all of which we have enumerated in Kifayat al-Muntaha.
Commentary: According to us, the ruling of rahn is that the rahn is detained in lieu of debt so that the mortgagee can recover his debt through it, because the mortgagee must have the right of recovery (yad al-istifa). According to Imam al-Shafi'i, the debt is attached to the collateral itself, not its value, and that is only by way of sale. Then upon this general principle branch many detailed issues, which the author says he has explained in Kifayat al-Muntaha. Then here the author presents one specific issue: according to our principle, since the mortgagee has a permanent right of detention until payment, if the mortgagor wants to take back the collateral, he cannot, otherwise the purpose of permanent detention would be lost. According to al-Shafi'i's principle, the mortgagor is not prevented from taking it back because that does not affect the purpose of sale. Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute explaining the fundamental difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the nature of rahn. The Hanafi school views rahn as a detention of the collateral (mahbus) to secure the debt, giving the mortgagee a right of recovery (yad al-istifa). The Shafi'i school views the debt as attaching to the collateral itself (ta'alluq al-dayn bi al-'ayn), enabling sale of the collateral for recovery. The author notes that many detailed issues branch from these two principles and that he has enumerated them in his work Kifayat al-Muntaha. He then illustrates with an example: if the mortgagor wishes to reclaim the collateral, the Hanafi principle prevents it because it would destroy the purpose of permanent detention, while the Shafi'i principle allows it because the collateral still serves as a means of sale. This difference in foundational understanding leads to distinct rulings in many related issues.

Key Terms
ید استیفاء (yad al-istifa): The right of recovery or taking possession to satisfy a debt.
محبوس (mahbus): The detained collateral in the context of rahn.
تعلق الدین بالعین (ta'alluq al-dayn bi al-'ayn): Attachment of the debt to the collateral itself, a Shafi'i concept.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the nature of rahn?
A) The debt attaches to the collateral itself.
B) The collateral is detained for the debt with right of recovery.
C) The collateral is sold immediately upon contract.
D) The mortgagor may reclaim the collateral anytime.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi and Shafi'i schools differ fundamentally on the nature of rahn: Hanafi views it as permanent detention for recovery, while Shafi'i views it as a temporary attachment for sale.

Rahn Valid Only for Guaranteed Debt
Ruling statement with rationale from al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of rahn and explain why only a guaranteed debt qualifies, using the concept of yad al-istifa.

Core Idea
Rahn is valid only for a guaranteed debt because recovery follows obligation.

This passage from al-Quduri's matn lays down a fundamental condition for the validity of rahn (mortgage/pledge) in Hanafi fiqh. It states that rahn is only valid when given for a guaranteed debt, and provides the logical basis: the purpose of rahn is to give the mortgagee the right of recovery, which can only exist after the debt is due.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the first sentence: رهن is not valid except for a guaranteed debt (دین مضمون). This is the main ruling.
Ruling is stated as a condition of validity.
2
Parse the condition
Determine what 'guaranteed debt' means. The commentary explains it as a debt that is fixed and obligatory, not contingent or future.
The term is emphatic; some scholars require the debt to be currently due.
3
Understand the rationale (talil)
The passage gives the reason: because the purpose of rahn is to establish the right of recovery (yad al-istifa), and recovery only follows after the debt has become obligatory (wujub).
This is a legal cause (illah) that explains the condition.
4
Analyze the emphasis and nuance
The phrase 'guaranteed debt' is emphatic since all debts are guaranteed. Some scholars interpret it to mean a debt currently due, excluding future or contingent debts.
This nuance affects cases like rahn for a guarantee of loss (daman bi al-darak).
5
Apply to examples
Consider whether a rahn given for a debt payable in one year is valid (yes, if debt is fixed). Consider a rahn given as security for a potential loss (no, if loss has not become a due debt).
The condition is about the nature of the debt, not the collateral.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا يصح الرهن الا بدین مضمون لان حكمه ثبوت يد الاستيفاء والاستيفاء يتلو الوجوب
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور رہن صحیح نہ ہوگا مگر دین مضمون کے بدلہ میں اس لئے کہ اس کا حکم ید استیفاء کا ثبوت ہے اور وصولیابی وجوب کے پیچھے آتی ہے۔
تشریح رہن صرف دین ہی کے بدلہ میں صحیح ہوتا ہے کیونکہ رہن کا حکم یہ ہے کہ مرتہن کو رہن پر ایسا قبضہ حاصل ہو جائے جس سے وہ اپنا قرض وصول کر سکے اور وصول جب کر سکے گا جب پہلے سے وجوب دین ثابت ہو چکا ہو۔
تنبیه دین مضمون ہی ہوتا ہے تو پھر دین کو مضمون کی قید سے مقید کرنا بطریق تاکید ہے اور بعض حضرات نے کہا کہ دین مضمون سے قدوری کی مراد وہ دین ہے جو فی الحال واجب ہو ورنہ ضمان بالدرک کے بدلہ رہن صحیح نہیں ہے۔
He said: Rahn is not valid except for a guaranteed debt, because its ruling is the establishment of the right of recovery, and recovery follows obligation.
Translation: Quduri said: Rahn is not valid except for a guaranteed debt, because its ruling is the establishment of the right of recovery, and recovery follows obligation.
Commentary: Rahn is only valid for a debt, because the ruling of rahn is that the mortgagee must obtain such possession of the collateral that he can recover his debt, and he can only recover when the obligation of the debt has been established beforehand.
Note: A guaranteed debt is itself debt, so restricting debt to guaranteed is by way of emphasis. Some said that by 'guaranteed debt' Quduri meant debt that is currently due; otherwise, rahn for guarantee of a potential loss (daman bi al-darak) is not valid.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn of al-Quduri, with commentary. The ruling: rahn is only valid for a guaranteed debt (dayn madmun). The rationale: the purpose of rahn is to give the mortgagee the right of recovery (yad al-istifa), and recovery can only occur after the debt has become obligatory (wujub). Therefore, the debt must be a fixed, guaranteed obligation. The note (tanbih) clarifies that 'guaranteed debt' is essentially redundant (since all debt is guaranteed), so it is emphatic. Some scholars interpret it to mean a debt that is currently due (hal), not future or contingent, so rahn for guarantee of loss (daman bi al-darak) is not valid according to this interpretation.

Key Terms
دین مضمون (dayn madmun): A debt that is guaranteed (i.e., fixed and obligatory).
ید استیفاء (yad al-istifa): Right of recovery; the mortgagee's right to take possession to recover debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is rahn only valid for a guaranteed debt according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because rahn is a gift.
B) Because recovery follows obligation, and rahn gives the right of recovery.
C) Because the collateral must be sold.
D) Because only guaranteed debts exist.

Key Takeaway
Rahn is only valid for a guaranteed debt because the mortgagee's right of recovery (yad al-istifa) depends on the debt being obligatory.

The Primary Obligation: Value as Debt in Guaranteed Objects
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of rahn for guaranteed objects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school validates rahn for guaranteed objects (a'yan madmuna) by distinguishing between the primary obligation (value) and the release of the object.

Core Idea
The primary obligation in guaranteed objects is value (debt), not the object itself; thus rahn is for a debt.

This passage addresses an apparent contradiction: Quduri stated rahn is only for a debt, yet the Hanafi school validates rahn for guaranteed objects like usurped goods. The resolution hinges on identifying the true nature of the obligation as value (debt).

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Recognize that Quduri's matn says rahn is only valid for a guaranteed debt, but the author raises an objection from the validity of rahn for a'yan madmuna (guaranteed specific objects) which are not debts per se.
Quduri's wording is the basis of the objection.
2
Recognize the Hanafi response
The response states that the primary obligator (mujib asli) in a'yan madmuna is the value (qima), which is a debt, and returning the specific object is a release (khilasan). So rahn is for the debt of value.
This distinction resolves the apparent contradiction.
3
Understand the distinction
Distinguish between what is fundamentally owed (the value, a debt) and the method of discharge (returning the object).
4
Support via analogy to suretyship
The text notes that suretyship (kafala) for such objects is valid, and kafala is only valid for debts, confirming that a debt aspect exists.
Analogy (qiyas) strengthens the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رضى الله عنه ويدخل على هذا اللفظ الرهن بالاعيان المضمونة بانفسها فانه يصح الرهن بها ولا دين
ترجمہ مصنف نے فرمایا اور قدوری کے اس لفظ پر ان اعیان سے اشکال وارد ہوتا ہے جو بذات خود مضمون ہیں کہ ان کے بدلہ میں رہن صحیح ہے حالانکہ دین نہیں ہے۔
تشریح امام قدوری نے مفرمایا کہ رہن صرف دین کے بدلہ میں صحیح ہوتا ہے اس پر صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جو چیز دین نہیں بلکہ عین ہیں اور ان کا ضمان واجب ہوتا ہے تو ان کے بدلہ میں رہن صحیح ہوتا ہے حالانکہ وہاں دین نہیں ہے تو بغیر دین کے رہن صحیح ہو گیا لہذا قدوری کا حصر غلط ہو گیا مثلاً زید نے خالد کا گھوڑہ غصب کر لیا تو زید پر اس کا ضمان واجب ہے اسی طرح جو چیز سوم شراء کے طریقہ پر مقبوض ہو اس کا ضمان واجب ہے جب ضمان واجب ہوا تو ان کے بدلہ رہن صحیح ہو گا تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں بغیر دین کے رہن درست ہوا جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ قدوری کا حصر مذکور صحیح نہیں ہے یہ اعتراض مکمل ہوا آگے مصنف اس کا جواب دیں گے۔
سوال مذکورہ کا جواب
يمكن ان يقال ان الموجب الاصلى فيها القيمة ورد العين مخلص على ما عليه اكثر المشائخ وهو دين ولهذا تصح الكفالة بها
ترجمہ اور ممکن ہے کہ جواب دیا جائے کہ ان میں (اعیان مضمونہ میں ) موجب اصلی قیمت ہے اور عین کو واپس کرنا چھٹکارا ہے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس پر اکثر مشائخ ہیں اور قیمت دین ہے اور اسی وجہ سے ان کی کفالت صحیح ہے۔
تشریح مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ اشکال مذکور کا یہ جواب دیا جا سکتا ہے جو اکثر مشائخ کی تقریر کے مطابق ہے کہ اعیان میں بھی اصل قیمت ہی واجب ہوتی ہے البتہ وہ اگر عین مغصوب کو واپس کر دے اس سے بھی وہ بری الذمہ ہو جائے گا اور قیمت دین ہے نہ کہ عین جب اس کا دین ہونا ثابت ہو گیا تو معلوم ہوا کہ رہن دین کے بدلہ میں ہے نہ کہ عین کے فلا اشکال اور اعیان مضمونہ کی کفالت بالاتفاق صحیح ہے اور کفالت دین کی صحیح ہوا کرتی ہے اس سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ اعیان مضمونہ میں دین کی جھلک موجود ہے۔
ایک اشکال کا جواب
ولئن كان لا تجب الا بعد الهلاك ولكنه تجب عند الهلاك بالقبض السابق ولهذا تعتبر قيمته يوم القبض فيكون رهنا بعد وجود سبب وجوبه فيصح كما في الكفالة
ترجمہ اگر چہ قیمت واجب نہیں ہوتی مگر ہلاکت کے بعد لیکن قیمت واجب ہوتی ہے ہلاکت کے وقت سابق قبضہ کی وجہ سے اسی وجہ سے مغصوب کی قیمت قبضہ کے دن کی معتبر ہوتی ہے پس مغصوب کے بدلہ میں رہن ہو گا اس کے سبب وجوب کے پائے جانے کے بعد
He said (may Allah be pleased with him): And under this wording enters rahn for guaranteed objects themselves, for rahn is valid for them even though there is no debt.
Translation: The author said: Objection arises to Quduri's wording from those objects which are guaranteed in themselves, for rahn is valid for them even though there is no debt.
Commentary: Imam Quduri said rahn is only valid for a debt. On this, the author of Hidayah says: For things that are not debts but are specific objects and their guarantee is obligatory, rahn is valid for them even though there is no debt. So rahn without debt became valid, indicating Quduri's restriction is incorrect. For example, Zayd usurped Khalid's horse; Zayd is liable for its guarantee. Similarly, something received with defective contract has its guarantee obligatory. When guarantee is obligatory, rahn is valid for them. So in these two cases, rahn without debt is valid, showing Quduri's restriction is not correct. This completes the objection; the author will answer it.
Answer to the objection:
It can be said that the primary obligator in them is the value, and returning the specific object is a release, according to what most mashayikh hold, and value is a debt, hence suretyship (kafala) is valid for it.
Translation: It is possible to answer that the primary obligator in these (guaranteed objects) is the value, and returning the specific object is a release, according to the detail held by most mashayikh, and the value is a debt, hence their suretyship is valid.
Commentary: The author says this objection can be answered according to the exposition of most mashayikh: the primary obligation in guaranteed objects is the value (qima), but if the usurped object is returned, that also discharges liability. The value is a debt, not the specific object. So when it is established that value is a debt, then rahn is for a debt, not for a specific object, so no objection. Moreover, suretyship (kafala) for guaranteed objects is unanimously valid, and suretyship is only valid for a debt, indicating that guaranteed objects involve a aspect of debt.
Answer to another objection:
Even though the value is not obligatory except after destruction, but it becomes obligatory at destruction due to prior possession, so the value at the day of possession is considered; thus rahn for usurped property will be after the existence of its cause of obligation, so it is valid, just as in suretyship.
Translation: Even though the value is not obligatory except after destruction, but it becomes obligatory at the time of destruction because of the prior possession, hence its value on the day of possession is considered; so rahn for usurped property will be after the existence of its cause of obligation, so it is valid, as in suretyship.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute. The author raises an objection to Quduri's statement that rahn is only for a debt: rahn is valid for guaranteed objects (a'yan madmuna) like usurped goods, even though there is no debt at the time of rahn. The author of Hidayah points out that such rahn is valid, which seems to contradict Quduri's restriction. The response is given: the primary obligation in such cases is actually the value (qima), which is a debt, but the return of the specific object is a release (khilasan). Since the value is a debt, rahn is for a debt, not a specific object, so the objection is resolved. Furthermore, suretyship for these objects is valid, confirming that debt is involved. A second objection: the value is not due until destruction, but the value becomes due at destruction based on prior possession, so rahn for the usurped object after the cause of obligation (possession) is valid, similar to suretyship for a future debt. Thus, the ruling that rahn is only for a debt holds, even for guaranteed objects.

Key Terms
اعیان مضمونہ (a'yan madmuna): Specific objects that are guaranteed (i.e., liability for them is obligatory, such as usurped goods).
موجب اصلی (mujib asli): Primary obligation; in case of a'yan madmuna, it is the value (qima), not the object itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is rahn for usurped goods (a'yan madmuna) valid?
A) Because usurped goods are considered debts
B) Because the primary obligation is the value, which is a debt
C) Because rahn is valid for any property
D) Because the usurped goods are returned later

Key Takeaway
Rahn for guaranteed objects (a'yan madmuna) is valid because the underlying obligation is the value (debt), not the specific object.

Timing of Obligation: Rahn for Future Debts via Prior Possession
Intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of debt obligation in rahn for guaranteed objects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle that a cause (sabab) of obligation can validate a rahn for a future debt, as established by the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Rahn for a future debt is valid when its cause (sabab) already exists, just like suretyship for future debt.

A second objection to rahn for a'yan madmuna is that the value is not due until destruction, so at the time of rahn, there is no existing debt. The Hanafi response uses the concept of sabab (cause) to validate rahn before the full obligation matures.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the second objection
Identify that the value of a'yan madmuna is only due upon destruction, so at the time of rahn, no debt exists.
This objection challenges the timing, not the nature of the obligation.
2
Understand the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response states that the value becomes obligatory at destruction due to prior possession. The cause (sabab) of the debt already exists from the moment of possession.
The cause is the unlawful possession that creates liability.
3
Compare to suretyship
Suretyship (kafala) for a future debt is valid when the cause of the debt exists; likewise, rahn for a'yan madmuna is valid after the cause.
Analogy (qiyas) is the basis for this reasoning.
4
Conclude
Therefore, rahn for a'yan madmuna is valid even before destruction because the cause of the debt is present.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمہ مصنف نے فرمایا اور قدوری کے اس لفظ پر ان اعیان سے اشکال وارد ہوتا ہے جو بذات خود مضمون ہیں کہ ان کے بدلہ میں رہن صحیح ہے حالانکہ دین نہیں ہے۔

Mortgage for Guaranteed Objects Is Valid Despite No Debt
Objection and resolution on mortgage for guaranteed objects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits mortgage for guaranteed objects and evaluate the proof based on the value being a debt.

Core Idea
A mortgage can be given for a guaranteed object because the primary obligation is its value, which is a debt.

This passage tackles a crucial question: can a mortgage (rahn) be given for something that is not a debt, such as a usurped object? Imam Qudūrī's statement that mortgage is only valid for a debt seems to exclude such cases. The author of al-Hidāyah resolves this by showing that the value of a guaranteed object is itself a debt, thus the rule holds.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Apparent Conflict
Compare Qudūrī's statement that mortgage is only for a debt with the established validity of mortgage for guaranteed objects (like usurped goods). What seems contradictory?
The conflict arises because the object itself is not a debt, yet mortgage is valid.
2
Locate the Hanafi Response
The majority of mashāyikh hold that in guaranteed objects, the primary obligation is the value (qīma), which is a debt. Returning the object is a release, not the primary duty.
This transforms the object into a debt-based obligation.
3
Analyze the Proof: Kafāla Analogy
Kafāla (suretyship) for guaranteed objects is unanimously valid. Since kafāla is only valid for a debt, this proves the value is a debt.
The sharia does not allow suretyship for a non-debt object.
4
Analyze the Proof: Hawāla Evidence
If a hawāla (transfer of debt) is tied to a usurped object, it remains valid after destruction, because the underlying value obligation (debt) persists. This contrasts with a deposit where no debt exists.
This confirms that the value is the primary obligation.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence
Mortgage can be given for a usurped object even before its destruction, because the cause of the value obligation (possessing the object) exists from the moment of possession.
Thus, the mortgage is valid from the start, not only after destruction.

ایک اشکال کا جواب
ولئن كان لا تجب الا بعد الهلاك ولكنه تجب عند الهلاك بالقبض السابق ولهذا تعتبر قيمته يوم القبض فيكون رهنا بعد وجود سبب وجوبه فيصح كما في الكفالة
ترجمہ اگر چہ قیمت واجب نہیں ہوتی مگر ہلاکت کے بعد لیکن قیمت واجب ہوتی ہے ہلاکت کے وقت سابق قبضہ کی وجہ سے اسی وجہ سے مغصوب کی قیمت قبضہ کے دن کی معتبر ہوتی ہے پس مغصوب کے بدلہ میں رہن ہو گا اس کے سبب وجوب کے پائے جانے کے بعد پر رہن صحیح ہوگا جیسے کفالت میں ہے۔

تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ اگر چہ بات یونہی ہے جیسے آپ نے فرمایا لیکن ہلاکت کے وقت جب قیمت واجب ہوئی اس کے وجوب کا سبب وہی قبضہ سابقہ ہے، اور یہی وجہ ہے کہ مغصوب کی وہی قیمت معتبر ہوگی جو قبضہ کے دن اس کی قیمت تھی لہذا جب بات یوں ہے تو معلوم ہوا کہ وجوب قیمت کا سبب غاصبانہ قبضہ کرتے ہی ثابت ہو گیا تو رہن غصب کے بدلہ میں دین کے سبب وجوب کے پائے جانے کے بعد ہوا ہے اور اس نکتہ کی وجہ سے اعیان مضمونہ کی کفالت صحیح ہوتی ہے کیونکہ یہ فی الجملہ وجوب قیمت تک موصل ہے۔
اعیان مضمونہ میں اصل قیمت واجب ہے
ولهذا لا تبطل الحوالة المقيدة به بهلاكه بخلاف الوديعة ترجمہ اور اسی وجہ سے (یعنی اعیان میں موجب اصل قیمت ہونے کی وجہ سے ) وہ حوالہ باطل نہ ہوگا جو عین مغصوب کے ساتھ مقید ہو مغصوب کے ہلاک ہونے کی وجہ سے بخلاف ودیعت کے۔
تشریح جب یہ معلوم ہو گیا کہ اعیان مضمونہ میں اصل قیمت واجب ہے تو اب سنئے زید نے خالد کی گھڑی غصب کر لی اور خالد کے ذمہ بکر کا قرض ہے خالد نے حوالہ کر دیا کہ میرا قرض زید دے گا یعنی گھڑی سے اس کا قرض ادا کرے گا اور اتفاق سے زید غاصب کے پاس سے گھڑی ہلاک ہوگئی تو حوالہ باطل نہ ہوا اور زید گھڑی کی قیمت سے دین مذکور کو ادا کرے گا اور اگر بعینہ یہی صورت ہو لیکن زید کے پاس بجائے غصب کے امانت ہو تو امانت کے ہلاک ہو جانے سے حوالہ باطل ہو جائے گا کیونکہ امانت میں جو حوالہ معین امانت کے ساتھ ہے تو عین کے ہلاک ہو جانے سے حوالہ باطل ہو جائے گا اور پہلی مثال میں عین کی ہلاکت سے حوالہ باطل نہ ہوگا کیونکہ موجب اصلی قیمت موجود ہے۔
Note: A debt is guaranteed, so restricting the word 'debt' with 'guaranteed' is by way of emphasis. Some scholars said that by 'guaranteed debt' Quduri means a debt that is due immediately, otherwise mortgage for the guarantee of compensation (damān al-darak) is not valid. Is mortgage valid in exchange for guaranteed objects? He (the author) says: And upon this wording, the objection enters regarding mortgage by guaranteed objects themselves, for it is valid to give them as mortgage while there is no debt. Commentary: Imam Quduri stated that mortgage is only valid for a debt. The author of al-Hidayah says: Things that are not debt but are objects, and their guarantee is obligatory, mortgage is valid in exchange for them even though there is no debt. So mortgage became valid without a debt, thus Quduri's restriction is wrong. For example, Zaid usurped Khalid's horse, so Zaid is liable for its guarantee. Similarly, something taken by way of purchase is guaranteed. When guarantee becomes obligatory, mortgage is valid in exchange for them. So in both cases mortgage became valid without a debt, indicating that Quduri's above statement is not correct. This objection is complete. Next the author will answer this objection. Answer to the mentioned question: It can be said that the primary obligator in them is the value, and returning the object is a release, according to what most mashāyikh are upon, and that is a debt. For this reason, suretyship (kafāla) for them is valid. Commentary: The author says that this answer can be given, which is in accordance with the view of most mashāyikh, that in objects the primary obligation is the value. However, if he returns the usurped object, he is discharged. And the value is a debt, not the object. When its being a debt is established, it becomes clear that mortgage is for a debt, not for the object, so no objection. And suretyship for guaranteed objects is unanimously valid, and suretyship is only valid for a debt. This also shows that in guaranteed objects there is a reflection of debt. Answer to another objection: And if it (the value) is not obligatory except after destruction, however it becomes obligatory at the time of destruction due to the previous possession, and for this reason its value at the day of possession is considered. So it becomes a mortgage after the existence of the cause of its obligation, so it is valid, as in suretyship. Commentary: Here an objection arises: the value of the usurped object becomes obligatory after its destruction, and as long as the usurped object still exists, its return is necessary. So how is it correct to say the value is the primary obligator? The answer is: although that is the case, but when the value becomes obligatory at the time of destruction, its cause is that previous possession. And this is why the considered value is the one at the day of possession. So when this is understood, it becomes clear that the cause of obligation of value is established from the moment of usurping possession. So mortgage in exchange for usurpation occurred after the cause of obligation of debt existed, and due to this point suretyship for guaranteed objects is valid because it leads to obligation of value in some aspects. The primary obligation in guaranteed objects is the value: And for this reason, the transfer (hawāla) that is restricted by it (the object) is not invalidated by its destruction, unlike the deposit. Commentary: When it became clear that in guaranteed objects the primary obligation is the value, now hear: Zaid usurped Khalid's watch, and Khalid owes a debt to Bakr. Khalid made a transfer (hawāla) that Zaid will pay his debt from the watch. Coincidentally the watch was destroyed in Zaid's possession. Then the transfer is not invalidated, and Zaid will pay the mentioned debt from the value of the watch. If the same case but Zaid had the watch as a deposit (amāna) instead of usurpation, then upon destruction the transfer becomes invalid, because the transfer in deposit is tied to the specific object, so with the destruction of the object the transfer becomes invalid. In the first example, the transfer is not invalidated because the primary obligator (value) exists.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling-with-proof discussion within the Hanafi school regarding the validity of mortgage (rahn) when given in exchange for guaranteed objects (a'yān maḍmūna) rather than a debt. The passage begins with a note distinguishing Quduri's statement that mortgage is only for a debt, and some scholars interpret Quduri's 'guaranteed debt' as a debt due immediately. Then an objection is raised: mortgage is valid even for objects that are guaranteed by themselves (like usurped goods) even though there is no debt. The author of al-Hidayah points out that Quduri's restriction is incorrect because in such cases the object itself is not a debt but its guarantee is obligatory, and mortgage is valid for such guarantee. Examples: a usurped horse or goods taken by purchase. The objection is fully presented. Then the author provides an answer following the majority of mashāyikh: the primary obligation in such guaranteed objects is actually the value (qīma), which is a debt. Returning the object is a release from that obligation. Since the value is a debt, mortgage is valid for it. This is supported by the fact that suretyship (kafāla) for such objects is valid, and kafāla is only valid for a debt. A second objection is answered: although the value becomes obligatory only after destruction, its cause is the previous possession (qabḍ). Therefore, the value is considered as of the day of possession, and the mortgage becomes valid after the cause of obligation exists, similar to kafāla. Finally, evidence from hawāla (transfer of debt) is provided: if a transfer is made tied to a usurped object, it is not invalidated by the object's destruction because the primary obligation is the value (a debt). But if the object is a deposit (amāna), the transfer is invalidated upon destruction because there is no debt obligation. Thus, the ruling establishes that mortgage can be given for guaranteed objects because the primary obligation is the value (a debt).

Key Terms
عین مضمونہ (ʿayn maḍmūna): A specific physical object that is guaranteed, meaning the possessor is liable for its value if destroyed (e.g., usurped goods, goods taken by defective sale).
موجب اصلی (mūjib aṣlī): The primary obligator — the fundamental legal obligation that arises from the situation (here, the value of the guaranteed object).
کفالت (kafāla): Suretyship — a contract where a person guarantees the debt or obligation of another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi mashāyikh, why is mortgage valid for guaranteed objects (a'yān maḍmūna) even though there is no debt?
A) Because the object itself is considered a debt due to its guarantee
B) Because the primary obligation is the value of the object, which is a debt
C) Because Quduri allowed it explicitly
D) Because the mortgage contract does not require a debt

Key Takeaway
Mortgage for a guaranteed object is valid because the primary obligation is its value, which constitutes a debt.

The Mortgagee's Guarantee: Lesser of Value and Debt
Statement of the Hanafi rule on the guarantee scope of a mortgaged object

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on the guarantee of a mortgaged object and apply it to the three scenarios based on the relationship between the property's value and the debt.

Core Idea
The mortgagee's liability is capped at the lesser of the property's value and the debt — excess is a trust, shortfall is deducted.

This lesson presents a foundational rule from Imam al-Quduri's matn on mortgages (rahn). The rule clarifies the precise extent of the mortgagee's guarantee when the mortgaged object is destroyed in his possession. Understanding this rule is essential because it balances the rights of both parties and prevents unjust enrichment or loss.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Memorize the maxim: 'The mortgaged object is guaranteed to the lesser of its value and the debt.' This means the mortgagee's liability upon destruction is limited to whichever of the two amounts is smaller.
2
Scenario: Value equals debt
If the property's value is exactly equal to the debt, then upon destruction, the mortgagee is considered to have fully received the debt (istīfā'). No further claim exists.
The mortgagee becomes 'mustawfī' (one who has collected).
3
Scenario: Value exceeds debt
If the property is worth more than the debt, the mortgagee is liable for the debt amount only. The excess value is an amāna (trust) in his hands; if destroyed accidentally, he is not liable for the excess.
The guarantee is only to the extent that satisfaction can occur, which is the debt amount.
4
Scenario: Value is less than debt
If the property's value is less than the debt, then only that value is deducted from the debt. The mortgagee may still pursue the remaining debt from the mortgagor.
Satisfaction is to the extent of the actual financial value (māliyya).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مرہونہ شی مرتہن کی ضمانت میں داخل ہے کس مقدار میں داخل ہے قال وهو مضمون بالاقل من قيمته و من الدين فاذا هلک فی ید المرتهن وقيمته والدين سواء صار المرتهن مستوفيا لدينه وان كانت قيمة الرهن اكثر فالفضل امانة لان المضمون بقدر ما يقع به الاستيفاء وذاك بقدر الدين فان كانت اقل سقط من الدين بقدره ورجع المرتهن بالفضل لان الاستيفاء بقدر المالية ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور مرہون مضمون ہوتا ہے رہن کی قیمت اور قرض میں سے اقل کے ساتھ پس جب کہ مرہون ہلاک ہو گیا مرتہن کے قبضہ میں اور اس کی قیمت اور قرض برابر ہوں تو ہو جائے گا مرتہن اپنے قرض کو وصول کرنے والا اور اگر رہن کی قیمت زیادہ ہو تو زیادتی امانت ہے اس لئے کہ مضمون اسی قدر ہو گا جس کے ذریعے وصولیابی واقع ہو سکے اور وہ ( وصولیابی ) بقدر قرض ہے پس اگر قیمت کم ہو تو قرض میں سے اسی کے بقدر ساقط ہو جائے گا اور مرتہن زیادتی کو واپس لے گا اس لئے کہ وصولیابی بقدر مالیت ہوتی ہے۔
The mortgaged object is included in the guarantee of the mortgagee. To what extent is it included? He (Quduri) said: It is guaranteed to the lesser of its value and the debt. So when it is destroyed in the hand of the mortgagee, and its value and the debt are equal, the mortgagee becomes one who has received his debt in full. If the value of the mortgage is more, the excess is a trust (amāna), because the guarantee is to the extent that satisfaction (of the debt) can take place, and that is to the amount of the debt. If it (the value) is less, then that amount of the debt falls, and the mortgagee pursues the remainder, because satisfaction (of the debt) is to the extent of the value.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This is a clear ruling statement from Quduri's matn on the extent of the mortgagee's guarantee regarding the mortgaged object. The rule is that the mortgaged object is guaranteed (i.e., if it is destroyed in the mortgagee's possession, the mortgagee is responsible) only up to the lesser of two amounts: the market value of the object at the time of destruction, and the outstanding debt. This has three scenarios: (1) If the value equals the debt, the mortgagee is considered to have fully collected the debt upon destruction — he owes nothing. (2) If the value exceeds the debt, the mortgagee is responsible for the value up to the debt amount; the excess value is held as a trust (amāna) for the mortgagor, meaning the mortgagee is not liable for it if it is destroyed accidentally. (3) If the value is less than the debt, the mortgagee is credited with that value against the debt, but he may still claim the remaining debt from the mortgagor. The underlying principle is that satisfaction (istīfā') of the debt can only occur to the extent of the value of the mortgaged property. This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
مضمون بالأقل (maḍmūn bi'l-aqall): Guaranteed to the lesser amount — the mortgagee's liability is limited to the lesser of the property's value and the debt.
استيفاء (istīfā'): Satisfaction or receipt of the debt in full, achieved when the value of the mortgage equals the debt upon destruction.
فضل (faḍl): Excess — the amount by which the mortgage's value exceeds the debt; held as a trust (amāna) by the mortgagee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mortgaged object worth $1000 is destroyed in the mortgagee's possession, and the debt is $800, what happens?
A) The mortgagee must pay $1000 to the mortgagor
B) The debt is considered fully paid, and the mortgagee owes nothing
C) $800 is deducted from the debt, and the mortgagee may claim the remaining $200 from the mortgagor
D) The mortgagee must return the excess $200 as a trust

Key Takeaway
The mortgagee's guarantee is limited to the lesser of the property's value and the debt; this determines whether the debt is fully satisfied, partially satisfied, or the mortgagee is a trustee for the excess.

Primary Obligation in Guaranteed Chattels and Its Effect on Hawala
Explaining that in guaranteed chattels, the price is the primary obligation from the moment of possession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the price of a guaranteed chattel is considered the primary obligation from the moment of possession and apply this ruling to determine the validity of a restricted hawala when the chattel is destroyed.

Core Idea
In guaranteed chattels, the price is wajib from the moment of possession, not only upon destruction.

This passage addresses a key Hanafi principle: the price of a guaranteed chattel (such as a usurped item) becomes an immediate obligation at the moment of possession, not at destruction. This has practical implications for transactions like hawala (debt transfer). By understanding this, you will grasp why a restricted hawala tied to a usurped item remains valid even after destruction, unlike a deposit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection
The passage poses an objection: since the price of a usurped item becomes due only after destruction, how can it be considered the primary obligation from the start? Recognize that this challenge assumes obligation arises only at destruction.
2
Understand the Response
The Hanafi response is that the cause of the price obligation (sabab al-wujub) is the initial wrongful possession, not the destruction. Therefore, the ruling of price being wajib is retroactively effective from the moment of possession.
3
Recognize the Cause of Obligation
The text argues that the price is considered the 'primary obligation' (mujib asli) because its cause—the usurping possession—is fixed at the time of taking. Thus, the price due is the value at that date.
4
Apply to Hawala Example
Work through the example: Zayd usurps Khalid's watch, Khalid transfers his debt to Bakr via hawala tied to the watch. The watch is destroyed. Since the watch's price was already wajib from the moment of usurpation, the hawala remains valid and Zayd must pay from that value. Contrast with a deposit: there the primary obligation is the chattel itself, so destruction invalidates the hawala.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح یہاں ایک اشکال وارد ہوتا ہے کہ قیمت مغصوب تو منصوب کی ہلاکت کے بعد ہوتی ہے اور جب تک شی مغصوب علی حال مجود ہے تو پھر اس کا واپس کرنا ضروری ہے تو قیمت کو موجب اصلی کہنا کیسے درست ہو گا ؟ تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ اگر چہ بات یونہی ہے جیسے آپ نے فرمایا لیکن ہلاکت کے وقت جب قیمت واجب ہوئی اس کے وجوب کا سبب وہی قبضہ سابقہ ہے، اور یہی وجہ ہے کہ مغصوب کی وہی قیمت معتبر ہوگی جو قبضہ کے دن اس کی قیمت تھی لہذا جب بات یوں ہے تو معلوم ہوا کہ وجوب قیمت کا سبب غاصبانہ قبضہ کرتے ہی ثابت ہو گیا تو رہن غصب کے بدلہ میں دین کے سبب وجوب کے پائے جانے کے بعد ہوا ہے اور نکتہ کی وجہ سے اعیان مضمونہ کی کفالت صحیح ہوتی ہے کیونکہ یہ فی الجملہ وجوب قیمت تک موصل ہے۔

اعیان مضمونہ میں اصل قیمت واجب ہے

ولهذا لا تبطل الحوالة المقيدة به بهلاكه بخلاف الوديعة

ترجمہ اور اسی وجہ سے (یعنی اعیان میں موجب اصل قیمت ہونے کی وجہ سے ) وہ حوالہ باطل نہ ہوگا جو عین مغصوب کے ساتھ مقید ہو مغصوب کے ہلاک ہونے کی وجہ سے بخلاف ودیعت کے۔

تشریح جب یہ معلوم ہو گیا کہ اعیان مضمونہ میں اصل قیمت واجب ہے تو اب سنئے زید نے خالد کی گھڑی غصب کر لی اور خالد کے ذمہ بکر کا قرض ہے خالد نے حوالہ کر دیا کہ میرا قرض زید دیگا یعنی گھڑی سے اس کا قرض ادا کرے گا اور اتفاق سے زید غاصب کے پاس سے گھڑی ہلاک ہوگئی تو حوالہ باطل نہ ہوا اور زید گھڑی کی قیمت سے دین مذکور کو ادا کرے گا اور اگر بعینہ یہی صورت ہو لیکن زید کے پاس بجائے غصب کے امانت ہو تو امانت کے ہلاک ہو جانے سے حوالہ باطل ہو جائے گا کیونکہ امانت میں جو حوالہ معین امانت کے ساتھ ہے تو عین کے ہلاک ہو جانے سے حوالہ باطل ہو جائے گا اور پہلی مثال میں مین کی ہلاکت سے حوالہ باطل نہ ہوگا کیونکہ موجب اصلی قیمت موجود ہے۔
Commentary: Here an objection arises: that the price of a usurped item becomes due only after its destruction, and as long as the usurped item is still in existence, its return is obligatory. So how can it be correct to say that the price is the primary obligation? The answer is given: although the matter is as you said, but at the time of destruction when the price became obligatory, its cause of obligation is that same prior possession. And this is why the price of the usurped item that is considered is the price it had on the day of possession. Therefore, when the matter is so, it becomes known that the cause of the obligation of price is established from the moment of usurpation. So the mortgage (rahn) occurs after the cause of obligation of the debt exists for the substitute of the usurpation. And because of this point, the guarantee (kafalah) of guaranteed chattels is valid, because it leads to the obligation of price in some respect. In guaranteed chattels, the original price is obligatory. And for this reason, the restricted hawala (transfer of debt) that is tied to the specific chattel does not become invalid due to its destruction, unlike the deposit. Translation: And for this same reason (i.e., because the original price is the cause in chattels), that hawala which is restricted to the specific usurped chattel will not become invalid due to the destruction of the usurped chattel, unlike the deposit. Commentary: When it became known that in guaranteed chattels the original price is obligatory, now listen: Zayd usurped Khalid's watch, and Khalid owed a debt to Bakr. Khalid made a hawala saying: 'Zayd will pay my debt, i.e., he will repay the debt from the watch.' And it so happened that the watch was destroyed in the hands of Zayd, the usurper. Then the hawala did not become invalid, and Zayd will pay the mentioned debt from the price of the watch. If the exact same situation occurred but Zayd had the watch as a deposit (amanah) instead of usurpation, then the deposit being destroyed would invalidate the hawala because in a deposit, the hawala is tied to the specific deposit. The destruction of the chattel invalidates the hawala. In the first example, the destruction of the chattel does not invalidate the hawala because the original price obligation exists.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, explaining that in guaranteed chattels (اعیان مضمونہ) such as those that are usurped or for which one is liable, the primary obligation is the original price (اصل قیمت) at the time of possession, not only after destruction. The author addresses an objection: how can the price be the primary obligation if it only becomes due upon destruction? The response is that the cause of obligation (سبب وجوب) is the initial wrongful possession itself, so the obligation is established from that moment. A practical application is given in hawala (transfer of debt): if a creditor transfers his debt to a usurper of his property, and the usurped property is destroyed, the hawala remains valid because that property's value is already due. However, if the property was held as a deposit (امانت), its destruction invalidates the hawala because the deposit's value is not inherently due. This distinction highlights the Hanafi principle that the cause of obligation in guaranteed chattels is the original possession, not destruction.

Key Terms
اعیان مضمونہ (a'yan mazmunah): Chattels that are guaranteed, meaning items for which one is liable to pay the value if destroyed, such as usurped goods or defective items in a contract.
موجب اصلی (mujib asli): The primary cause or obligation; here it refers to the original price being the fundamental liability in guaranteed chattels.
حوالہ مقید (hawalah muqayyadah): A restricted transfer of debt tied to a specific item, where the debt is to be paid from that specific property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example given, why does the hawala (transfer of debt) remain valid when the usurped item is destroyed?
A) Because the hawala was not tied to the specific item
B) Because the usurper had already consumed the item
C) Because the price of the usurped item is considered the primary obligation from the time of usurpation
D) Because the creditor waived his right to the item

Key Takeaway
The price of a guaranteed chattel is wajib from the moment of possession, so a restricted hawala tied to such a chattel remains valid even after its destruction.

The Extent of Guarantee for a Pledged Item
Stating and explaining the ruling that the pledged property is guaranteed by the lesser of its value or the debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the extent of guarantee for a pledged item and apply it to three scenarios (value equals, exceeds, or falls short of the debt).

Core Idea
A pledge is guaranteed only by the lesser of its value or the debt, protecting both parties from unfair gain.

In this lesson, we examine the precise extent to which a pledged item (marhun) is guaranteed (maznun) in the hands of the mortgagee (murtahin). The Hanafi school establishes a unique principle: the guarantee is limited to the lesser of the item's value and the debt. This prevents the mortgagee from profiting beyond the debt and ensures the mortgagor's liability does not exceed the collateral's worth. We will explore three scenarios that clarify how this rule is applied in practice.

Guided Path
1
Understand the base rule
The pledge is guaranteed by the lesser of its value and the debt. This is the core principle from al-Quduri's matn.
2
Analyze scenario 1: value equals debt
If the pledged item's value equals the debt, and it is destroyed in mortgagee's custody, the mortgagee is considered to have recovered the debt fully.
The mortgagee cannot claim more.
3
Analyze scenario 2: value exceeds debt
If value is greater, the guarantee covers only the debt amount. The excess is held as a trust (amanah) for the mortgagor, and the debt is considered paid.
The mortgagee must return the excess if still existent, or its value if destroyed.
4
Analyze scenario 3: value is less than debt
If value is less, the debt is reduced by the value of the destroyed item. The mortgagee can claim the remaining debt from the mortgagor.
The mortgagee bears the loss of the difference.
5
Apply the rule to new scenarios
Given any two numbers (value and debt), state which is lesser and determine the guarantee amount and resulting obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح ماقبل میں بتایا جا چکا ہے کہ مرہون مرتہن کی ضمانت میں داخل ہو گا اب اس پر یہ سوال پیدا ہو گا کہ کس مقدار میں مضمون ہوگا ؟ تو یہاں اس کا جواب دیا ہے کہ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ رہن کی قیمت اور قرض میں جو بھی کم ہو اسی مقدار کے ساتھ مضمون ہو گا لہذا اگر رہن کی قیمت دو سوروپے ہو اور قرض سوروپے ہو تو سوروپے کم ہیں اور رہن کی قیمت زیادہ ہے تو اس صورت میں ضمان بقد رسوروپے ہوگا اور اگر اس کے برعکس ہو تب بھی ضمان بقد ر سو روپے ہوگا۔

مرہونہ شی مرتہن کی ضمانت میں داخل ہے کس مقدار میں داخل ہے قال وهو مضمون بالاقل من قيمته و من الدين فاذا هلک فی ید المرتهن وقيمته والدين سواء صار المرتهن مستوفيا لدينه وان كانت قيمة الرهن اكثر فالفضل امانة لان المضمون بقدر ما يقع به الاستيفاء وذاك بقدر الدين فان كانت اقل سقط من الدين بقدره ورجع المرتهن بالفضل لان الاستيفاء بقدر المالية

ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور مرہون مضمون ہوتا ہے رہن کی قیمت اور قرض میں سے اقل کے ساتھ پس جب کہ مرہون ہلاک ہو گیا مرتبہن کے قبضہ میں اور اس کی قیمت اور قرض برابر ہوں تو ہو جائے گا مرتہن اپنے قرض کو وصول کرنے والا اور اگر رہن کی قیمت زیادہ ہو تو زیادتی امانت ہے اس لئے کہ مضمون اسی قدر ہو گا جس کے ذریعے وصولیابی واقع ہو سکے اور وہ ( وصولیابی ) بقدر قرض ہے پس اگر قیمت کم ہو تو قرض میں سے اسی کے بقدر ساقط ہو جائے گا اور مرتہن زیادتی کو واپس لے گا اس لئے کہ وصولیابی بقدر مالیت ہوتی ہے۔

لہذا اگر مرتہن کے پاس مرہون ہلاک ہو گیا اور قرض اور رہن کی قیمت برابر ہو تو مسئلہ برابر سرابر ہے اور مرتہن اپنا قرض وصول کر لینے والا شمار ہوگا اور اگر رہن کی قیمت زیادہ ہو تو زیادتی امانت ہوگی اور قرض ادا ہو گیا کیونکہ مرتین جتنی مقدار سے اپنا قرض وصول کر سکے اتنی ہی مقدار مضمون ہوتی ہے اور وہ مقدار بقدر دین ہی ہے۔

اور اگر رہن کی قیمت کم ہو اور قرض زیادہ ہو تو جتنی رہن کی قیمت تھی رہن کے ہلاک ہونے سے اتنا قرض ساقط ہو گیا اور باقی قرض کو مرتهن راہن سے وصول کرے گا کیونکہ یہاں مرتہن کو اتنی مقدار کا وصول کرنے والا شمار کیا جائے گا جتنی رہن کی مالیت ہے۔
Commentary: It has been stated before that the pledged item enters into the guarantee of the mortgagee. Now a question arises: to what extent is it guaranteed? Here the answer is given, the gist of which is that the pledge is guaranteed by the lesser of its value and the debt. So if the value of the pledge is two hundred rupees and the debt is one hundred rupees, then one hundred is less and the value is more, so in that case the guarantee is to the extent of one hundred rupees. If the opposite is the case, then also the guarantee is to the extent of one hundred rupees. The pledged item enters into the guarantee of the mortgagee. To what extent? He (al-Quduri) said: It is guaranteed by the lesser of its value and the debt. So if it is destroyed in the hand of the mortgagee, and its value and the debt are equal, the mortgagee becomes one who has recovered his debt. If the value of the pledge is more, then the excess is a trust, because the guarantee is to the extent that recovery can be made, and that is to the extent of the debt. If it is less, then the debt is reduced by that amount, and the mortgagee claims the excess, because recovery is to the extent of value. Translation: Al-Quduri stated: The pledged item is guaranteed by the lesser of its value and the debt. So when it is destroyed in the hand of the mortgagee, if its value and the debt are equal, the mortgagee becomes one who has recovered his debt. If the value of the pledge is more, then the excess is a trust, because the guarantee is only to the extent that recovery can take place, and that is to the extent of the debt. If it is less, then the debt is reduced by its amount, and the mortgagee takes the excess (from the mortgagor) because recovery is to the extent of the monetary value. Therefore, if the pledged item is destroyed in the hand of the mortgagee, and the debt and the value of the pledge are equal, then the matter is equal, and the mortgagee is considered to have recovered his debt. If the value of the pledge is more, then the excess is a trust, and the debt is paid, because the mortgagee's guarantee is only to the extent that he can recover his debt, and that amount is to the extent of the debt. And if the value of the pledge is less and the debt is more, then to the extent of the pledge's value, that much of the debt is dropped due to its destruction, and the mortgagee will recover the remaining debt from the mortgagor, because here the mortgagee is considered to have recovered to the extent of the pledge's value.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of al-Quduri, explaining the principle that a pledged item (marhun) is guaranteed (maznun) by the mortgagee (murtahin) to the extent of the lesser (aqall) of its value or the debt. The commentary clarifies three scenarios: (1) If value equals debt, destruction extinguishes the debt and the mortgagee recovers fully. (2) If value exceeds debt, the excess is held as a trust (amanah) and must be returned to the mortgagor; the debt is considered paid. (3) If value is less than debt, the debt is reduced by the value of the destroyed item, and the mortgagee can claim the remainder from the mortgagor. This ruling ensures that the mortgagee does not gain more than his due and the mortgagor's liability is limited to the actual value of the collateral.

Key Terms
مضمین (mazmūn): Guaranteed; the pledged item is covered by a guarantee (daman) in the hands of the mortgagee.
اقل (aqall): The lesser of two amounts; here it determines the extent of guarantee.
استيفاء (istīfā'): Recovery; the act of the mortgagee taking the debt from the pledge.
امانت (amānah): A trust; the excess value above the debt is not guaranteed but held in trust for the mortgagor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pledged item worth 200 rupees is destroyed in the mortgagee's custody, and the debt is 150 rupees, what happens?
A) The mortgagee recovers 150 rupees and the excess 50 is a trust for the mortgagor
B) The mortgagee recovers 200 rupees from the mortgagor
C) The debt is reduced to 50 rupees
D) The mortgagee receives nothing

Key Takeaway
The pledged item is guaranteed by the lesser of its value or the debt, ensuring fair recovery.

Imam Zufar's View: The Pledge is Guaranteed by Full Value
Presenting Imam Zufar’s dissenting opinion that the pledge is guaranteed by its full value, with his evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Zufar's position on the guarantee of a pledged item, identify his textual and rational evidence, and distinguish his view from the main Hanafi position.

Core Idea
Imam Zufar holds the entire pledged value is guaranteed, based on a hadith and analogy.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the extent to which a pledged item (rahn) is guaranteed in the hands of the mortgagee (murtahin). While the majority of the Hanafi school, led by Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, holds that the guarantee is limited to the lesser of the debt or the value, Imam Zufar argues that the full value is guaranteed. This difference has practical consequences when the pledge is destroyed and its value differs from the debt. We will explore Zufar's textual and rational proofs, and understand the practical implications of his view.

Guided Path
1
State the main Hanafi position
Recall that the main school says the pledge is guaranteed by the lesser of its value or the debt.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
State Imam Zufar's position
Zufar says it is guaranteed by the full value, regardless of the debt amount.
He is a major Hanafi authority, but his view is not the relied-upon one.
3
Examine Zufar's dalil naqli
Analyze the hadith of Ali (ra) 'yataraddan al-fadl' and how Zufar interprets it.
The hadith is ahad (zanni thubut) and its interpretation is disputed.
4
Examine Zufar's dalil aqli (qiyas)
Understand his analogy: the excess value is mortgaged just like the debt, so it should be guaranteed.
The main school objects that the excess is not held as security in the same way.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
امام زفر کا نقطہ نظر

وقال زفر الرهن مضمون بالقيمة حتى لوهلك الرهن وقيمته يوم رهن الف وخمسمائة والدين الف رجع الراهن على المرتهن بخمس مائة

ترجمہ اور زفر نے فرمایا کہ رہن قیمت کے ساتھ مضمون ہوتا ہے یہاں تک کہ اگر رہن ہلاک ہو جائے اور رہن کی قیمت رہن رکھنے کے دن پندرہ سو اور قرض ہزار ہو تو راہن مرتہن سے پانچ سو واپس لے گا۔

تشریح ہمارا مذ ہب وہ ہے جو گذر چکا امام زفر کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ رہن کی جو بھی قیمت ہو اس کے بقدر مرتہن پر ضمان ہوگالہذا اگر رہن رکھنے کے دن مرہون کی قیمت پندرہ سو روپے ہو اور قرض ایک ہزار روپیہ ہو اور رہن مرتبین کے ہاں ہلاک ہو جائے تو مرتہن کا قرض بھی ادا ہو گیا اور راہن مرتہن سے پانچ سوروپے واپس لے گا آگے امام زفر نے دلیل نقلی اور دلیل عقلی پیش فرمائی ہیں ۔

امام زفر کی دلیل

له حديث على رضى الله عنه قال يتراد ان الفضل في الرهن ولان الزيادة على الدين مرهونة لكونها محبوسة به فتكون مضمونة اعتبارا بقدر الدين

ترجمہ زفر کی دیں حضور علی کی حدیث ہے انہوں نے کہا ہے کہ دونوں راہن و مرتہن ) رہن میں زیادتی کا لین دین کریں گے اور اس لئے کہ رہن پر زیادتی مرہون ہے زیادتی کے محبوس ہونے کی وجہ سے دین کے بدلہ میں تو زیادتی مضمون ہوگی دین کی مقدار پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے ۔

تشریح یہ امام زفر کی دلیل ہے پہلی دلیل نقلی ہے کہ حضرت علی نے رہن کے بارے میں فرمایا ہے کہ را ہن اور مرتبین زیادتی کا لین دین کریں گے یعنی اگر قرض رہن سے زیادہ ہے تو زیادتی راہن سے لی جائے گی اور اگر رہن کی قیمت زیادہ ہے تو زیادتی مرتہن سے
Imam Zufar's viewpoint. And Zufar said: The pledge is guaranteed by the value, so much so that if the pledge is destroyed and its value on the day of pledge is one thousand five hundred and the debt is one thousand, the mortgagor takes back five hundred from the mortgagee. Translation: And Zufar stated that the pledge is guaranteed by the value, to the extent that if the pledge is destroyed and its value on the day of pledge is fifteen hundred and the debt is one thousand, then the mortgagor will get back five hundred from the mortgagee. Commentary: Our madhhab is what has passed. Imam Zufar's madhhab is that the pledge is guaranteed according to whatever its value is. Therefore, if on the day of pledge the value is fifteen hundred rupees and the debt is one thousand rupees, and the pledge is destroyed in the hands of the mortgagee, then the mortgagee's debt is paid and the mortgagor takes back five hundred rupees from the mortgagee. Next, Imam Zufar presents a textual proof and a rational proof. Imam Zufar's proof: He has a hadith from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: 'They mutually return the excess in the pledge.' And because the excess over the debt is mortgaged (marhun) due to being held as a security for the debt, so it is guaranteed, by analogy to the extent of the debt. Translation: Zufar's proof is the hadith of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: 'Both (the mortgagor and mortgagee) shall mutually exchange the excess in the pledge.' And because the excess over the debt is mortgaged due to being held as security for the debt, so the excess is guaranteed, drawing an analogy to the extent of the debt. Commentary: This is Imam Zufar's proof. The first proof is textual: that Hadrat Ali said regarding the pledge that the mortgagor and mortgagee shall mutually exchange the excess, meaning if the debt is more than the pledge, the excess will be taken from the mortgagor, and if the value of the pledge is more, the excess will be taken from the mortgagee.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage presents the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa (and the main madhhab) and Imam Zufar regarding the extent of guarantee on a pledged item. While the main madhhab holds that the pledge is guaranteed by the lesser of its value or the debt, Imam Zufar argues that it is guaranteed by its full value. His evidence includes: (1) A hadith from Ali (ra) stating that the parties mutually return the excess (فضیل) in a pledge. (2) A rational argument that the excess is also mortgaged (مرہون) because it is held as security for the debt, so by analogy (قیاس) to the debt itself, it should also be guaranteed. The commentary explains that according to Zufar, if the pledge's value exceeds the debt, the mortgagee is considered to have recovered his full debt, and the excess must be returned to the mortgagor. Conversely, if the debt exceeds the value, the mortgagor must pay the shortfall. The Hanafi response to Zufar's evidence is not given in this passage but is addressed elsewhere in the Hidayah.

Key Terms
زفر (Zufar): Imam Zufar, a prominent student of Abu Hanifa and a Hanafi jurist who held a dissenting view on this issue.
فضل (fadl): Excess; the surplus of the pledge's value over the debt, or vice versa.
یترادان (yatarāddān): They both mutually give back; from the hadith indicating that the parties exchange the excess.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the textual proof (dalil naqli) that Imam Zufar uses to support his view that the pledge is guaranteed by its full value?
A) A verse from the Quran about contracts
B) A hadith from Ali (ra) stating that parties mutually return the excess in the pledge
C) A consensus of the Companions
D) The practice of the people of Madinah

Key Takeaway
Imam Zufar's view that the pledge is guaranteed by its full value is a well-known intra-Hanafi opinion, but the relied-upon position is that the guarantee is limited to the lesser of the debt or the value.

Pledge Performance Order: Mortgagor Pays First
States that mortgagor pays debt first then mortgagee releases pledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a mortgagee produces the pledge, and apply the qiyas with sale to derive the order of performance.

Core Idea
Equality requires the mortgagor to pay first when the mortgagee produces the pledge.

This passage from the Hidayah addresses a procedural question in the contract of pledge (rahn). When the mortgagee (murtahin) produces the pledged property in court, should the mortgagor pay the debt first or should the mortgagee release the pledge first? The Hanafi ruling is clear: the mortgagor must pay the debt first. This is derived from the principle of equality (taswiyah) and analogized to the sale of goods.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal question
The mortgagee has produced the pledged property. The question is: which party must perform first – the mortgagor paying the debt, or the mortgagee releasing the pledge?
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The text explicitly rules that the mortgagor is ordered to pay the debt first, then the mortgagee releases the pledge.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
3
Recognize the underlying principle
The ruling is based on taswiyah (equality). The mortgagor already has a specific right in the pledge (a specific item), while the mortgagee's right to the debt is unspecific until payment. To make both rights specific, payment must come first.
This ensures fairness and clarity.
4
Follow the qiyas with sale
The author draws an analogy from sale: when the seller produces the goods (mabi'), the buyer pays the price (thaman) first. Similarly, in pledge, the mortgagee produces the pledge (like goods), and the mortgagor pays the debt (like price) first.
The illa (effective cause) is the need for specification and equality.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
A person pawns his watch for a loan. The pawnbroker produces the watch in court. The borrower must pay the debt first, then the pawnbroker returns the watch.
This illustrates the sequential performance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الرهن
واذا احضره امر الراهن بتسليم الدين اولا ليتعين حقه كما تعين حق الراهن تحقيقا للتسوية كما في تسليم المبيع والثمن يحضر المبيع ثم يسلم الثمن اولا ترجمہ اور جب مرتہن نے رہن کو حاضر کر دیا تو راہن کو اولاً قرض سپرد کرنے کا حکم دیا جائے گا تا کہ مرتین کا حق متعین ہو جائے ، جیسا کہ راہن کا حق متعین ہو گیا برابری کو ثابت کرنے کے لئے جیسا کہ مبیع اور شمن کے سپرد کرنے میں مبیع کو حاضر کیا جاتا ہے پھر پہلے شمن کو سپرد کیا جاتا ہے۔ تشریح. جب مرتهن مرہون کو حاضر کر دے تو چونکہ مرہون تو متعین چیز ہے جس میں راہن کا حق متعین ہے اور روپوں میں حق متعین نہیں ہے چونکہ وہ غیر معین ہیں اس لئے برابری کی غرض سے پہلے راہن اس کا قرض ادا کرے پھر مرتہن اس کے درالہ مرہون کو کریگا جیسا کہ مبیع اور شمن میں بھی یہی حکم ہے کہ پہلے شمن دیا جاتا ہے اس کے بعد مبیع حوالہ کیا جائیگا۔
Book of Pledge. When he produces it, the mortgagor is ordered to deliver the debt first so that his right is specified, just as the mortgagor's right was specified, to achieve equality, as in the delivery of the sold item and the price: the sold item is produced and then the price is delivered first.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Book of Pledge (Kitab al-Rahn). It addresses the procedure when the mortgagee (murtahin) produces the pledged property (marhun) in court. The ruling states that the mortgagor (rahin) is first ordered to pay the debt, thereby making the mortgagee's right definite, just as the mortgagor's right over the pledge was already specific (since the pledge is a specific item). This ensures equality between the two parties. The author draws an analogy from the law of sale: when the buyer and seller both appear, the seller must produce the goods first, then the buyer pays the price. Similarly, here the pledge is like the goods, and the debt is like the price; the mortgagor pays the debt first, then the mortgagee releases the pledge. The commentary elaborates that the pledge is a specific item (mu'ayyan) with a defined right for the mortgagor, while the debt is unspecified (ghayr mu'ayyan) in terms of its connection to the pledge, so payment must come first to achieve balance.

Key Terms
تسليم الدين (taslim al-dayn): Delivery/payment of the debt by the mortgagor to the mortgagee.
تسوية (taswiyah): Equal treatment between mortgagee and mortgagor by sequential performance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When the mortgagee produces the pledged property, what is the mortgagor ordered to do first?
A) Take possession of the pledge
B) Pay the debt
C) Produce the pledge again
D) Cancel the contract

Key Takeaway
When the mortgagee produces the pledge, Hanafi law requires the mortgagor to pay the debt first to achieve equality between the parties.
