Light vs Heavy Pledge: Demand in a Different City
Ruling on mortgagee demanding debt in a different city: light vs heavy pledges

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the distinction between light and heavy pledges to determine whether the mortgagee must produce the pledge when demanding debt in a different city.

Core Idea
A mortgagee's duty to produce the pledge depends on its portability: light items must be produced, heavy items need not.

Imagine a pledge made in one city but the debt is demanded in another. Must the mortgagee bring the pledged item to the new location? The Hanafi school answers this by looking at the nature of the pledge itself—whether it is easily transportable (لا حمل له ولا مؤنة) or heavy. This lesson unpacks that distinction, the proof from consensus in salam, and the qiyas that extends the same principle to pledges.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The mortgagee demands repayment of the debt in a city different from where the pledge contract was made.
2
Classify the pledge
Determine if the pledged item is 'light' (no burden/expense) or 'heavy' (has burden/expense).
Use criteria: can it be carried without significant effort or cost?
3
Apply the rule
If light, the mortgagee must produce the pledge before collecting debt. If heavy, he may collect without producing.
The same answer as when demand is in the same city for light pledges.
4
Understand the proof
The principle is supported by ijma in salam contracts, where place of delivery is not specified for light items, and by qiyas from that case to pledges.
The illa is the absence of burden/expense.
5
Distinguish delivery types
The mortgagee's obligation is taslim (surrender) through takhliyah (vacating possession), not physical transport (naql). For heavy items, transport causes extra harm not undertaken.
This prevents additional darar.

Source Text

And if he demands the debt in a city other than the one where the contract took place: if the pledge is of the type that has no burden and no expense, then the answer is the same because all places with respect to delivery are like one place for that which has no burden and expense. For this reason, in salam it is not required by consensus to specify the place of payment. And if it has burden and expense, he takes his debt and is not required to produce the pledge because this is transfer, and what is obligatory on him is delivery in the sense of relinquishment, not transfer from place to place, because he would suffer increased harm and he did not undertake that.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage expands on the previous ruling when the mortgagee demands payment in a different city from the contract. The key factor is whether the pledged property is easily transportable (no burden/hamal or expense/mu'nah). For light items (e.g., a watch, pen, ring), all places are equivalent for delivery; thus the same rule applies: the mortgagee must first produce the pledge. The author supports this by citing the consensus (ijma) in salam contracts where the place of delivery need not be specified for such items. For heavy items (e.g., large quantities of linen), the mortgagee is not required to produce the pledge; he can simply collect the debt. The reason is that the mortgagee's obligation is taslim (surrender) which means takhliyah (vacating possession), not physical transportation. Requiring transport would cause additional harm (darar) which he never agreed to. The Urud commentary illustrates with examples: Deoband and Delhi.

Key Terms
حمل (haml): Burden of carrying the pledge; used to determine if transportation is easy or difficult.
مؤنة (mu'nah): Expense or cost associated with transporting the pledge.
تخلیہ (takhliyah): Vacating possession; legal delivery without physical transfer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Mortgagee can collect the debt without producing the pledge
D) The contract becomes void

Key Takeaway
The mortgagee's obligation to produce the pledge in a different city depends on whether the pledge is light (must produce) or heavy (not required).

Absolute Authorization to the 'Adil: Valid Sale for Cash or Credit
Ruling on sale by 'adil with absolute authorization

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a mortgagor gives absolute authorization to the 'adil to sell the pledged property and explain why the sale is valid for both cash and credit, and why the mortgagee is not required to produce the pledge after the sale.

Core Idea
Absolute authorization empowers the 'adil to sell for cash or credit; the mortgagee's claim does not require producing the sold pledge.

In Hanafi muamalat law, the 'adil (trustee) holds the pledge by mutual consent. When the mortgagor gives the 'adil unrestricted permission to sell, the sale is valid regardless of payment method. This lesson breaks down the ruling and its implications, clarifying that the mortgagee's demand for repayment does not compel him to produce the pledge after sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and authority
Recognize that the mortgagor (rahin) has given the 'adil permission to sell the pledged property. Note that the permission is absolute (mutlaq) — no restriction on cash or credit.
The key term is 'taslit' (empowerment). Absolute means no conditions attached.
2
Derive the permissibility of credit sale
Because the authorization is unrestricted, it includes both cash (naqd) and credit (nasi'ah). The Hanafi principle: al-amr al-mutlaq yashmal al-jins — an absolute command includes all species.
If the mortgagor had specified 'cash only', the credit sale would be fasid (voidable) without his consent.
3
Understand the mortgagee's position after sale
The mortgagee (murtahin) may demand repayment of the debt from the mortgagor. However, since the pledge has been sold, the mortgagee no longer has physical power (qudrah) over it, so he is not required to produce it.
This protects the mortgagee from an impossible obligation — he cannot produce what he no longer possesses.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Imagine a pawnshop as 'adil. If the owner gives an absolute sale order, the pawnshop may sell the item for cash or on installment. After sale, the lender (mortgagee) can still ask the owner to repay, but cannot be forced to produce the item.
In modern finance, this applies to broker-held collateral with unrestricted sale authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و لو سلط الراهن العدل على بيع المرهون فباعه بنقد او نسيئة جاز لا طلاق الا مرفلو طالب المرتهن بالدين لا يكلف المرتهن احضار الرهن لانه لا قدرة له على الاحضار
ترجمہ اور اگر راہن نے عادل کو مرہون کے بیچنے پر مسلط کر دیا پس عادل نے اس کو نقد یا ادھار فروخت کر دیا تو جائز ہے حکم کے مطلق ہونے کی وجہ سے پس اگر مرتہن نے قرض کا مطالبہ کیا تو مرتہن رہن کو حاضر کرنے کا مکلف نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ مرتہن کو حاضر کرنے پر قدرت
نہیں ہے۔ تشریح عادل اس کو کہتے ہیں جس کے پاس با تفاق را ہن و مرتهن مرہون کو رکھدیا گیا ہے تو اگر راہن نے عادل کو کہا کہ مرہون کو بیچ دے تو چونکہ راہن کا حکم مطلق ہے لہذا یہ نقد اور ادھار دونوں کو شامل ہو گا لہذا عادل نے اگر اس کو ادھار فروخت کر دیا تو جائز ہے بہر حال اسی دوران مرتہن نے راہن سے اپنے قرض کا مطالبہ کیا تو اس کا مطالبہ حق بجانب ہے لیکن یہاں مرتہن کو یہ حکم نہ ہوگا کہ وہ پہلے رہن کو حاضر کرے کیونکہ مرتہن کو اب رہن کے حاضر کرنے کی قدرت نہیں ہے کماہو ظاہر
And if the mortgagor authorizes the 'adil to sell the pledged property, and he sells it for cash or credit, it is permissible because of the absoluteness of the command. And if the mortgagee demands the debt, the mortgagee is not required to produce the pledge because he has no power to produce it.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling regarding the 'adil (trustee) who holds the pledge by agreement of both parties. If the mortgagor gives the 'adil absolute permission to sell the pledge, the 'adil can sell it for either cash or credit (deferred payment) — both are valid because the authorization was unrestricted (mutlaq). However, if during this period the mortgagee demands repayment of the debt from the mortgagor, the mortgagee is not obligated to produce the pledge (which is now sold and no longer in his possession or power). The reason is that the mortgagee lacks physical power (qudrah) over the pledge after the sale. The commentary emphasizes that 'adil is the one with possession by mutual consent.

Key Terms
عدل ('adil): A trustworthy third party who holds the pledged property by mutual agreement of mortgagor and mortgagee.
تسليط (taslit): Granting authority or empowerment to act, here specifically to sell.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Valid only if mortgagee consents
C) Valid because the authorization is absolute
D) Valid only if cash

Key Takeaway
Absolute authorization to the 'adil makes the sale valid for both cash and credit, and the mortgagee is not bound to produce the pledge after the sale.

The Substitute Ruling in Mortgage (Rahn)
Ruling when mortgagee sells pledge by mortgagor's order: effect on production duty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle 'al-badl qa'im maqam al-mubdal' to determine when a mortgagee must produce the sale price before collecting the debt.

Core Idea
The price replaces the pledge; production duty transfers to the substitute.

When a mortgagor authorizes the mortgagee to sell the pledged item, the mortgagee may either take possession of the sale price or leave it as a debt. Hanafi fiqh distinguishes these two scenarios. This lesson focuses on the case where the mortgagee takes physical possession of the price, establishing a clear duty to produce it when demanding repayment. The ruling is derived by qiyas (analogy) from the original duty to produce the physical pledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify possession status
First, determine whether the mortgagee took possession of the price after selling the pledge with permission. The ruling depends on this fact.
2
Apply substitute principle
If he took possession, recognize that the price stands in place of the original pledge. The rule 'al-badl qa'im maqam al-mubdal' transfers the legal duty from the specific item to its monetary substitute.
This is a key principle in Hanafi muamalat.
3
Trace the qiyas (analogy)
The original case: the mortgagee must produce the physical pledge before demanding debt. The new case: after sale and possession of price, the price is the substitute. The effective cause (illa) is that both are security for the debt. Therefore, the same duty applies.
See the qiyas panel in the commentary.
4
Confirm the contractor's role
The mortgagee is the contracting party in the sale, so he collects the price. His duty to produce mirrors his duty to produce the original pledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا اذا امر المرتهن ببيعه فباعه ولم يقبض الثمن لانه صاردينا بالبيع بامر الراهن فصار كان الراهن رهنه وهو دين ولو قبضه يكلف احضاره لقيام البدل مقام المبدل الا ان الذى يتولى قبض الثمن هو المرتهن لانه هو العاقد فترجع الحقوق اليه وكما يكلف احضار الرهن لا ستيفاء كل الدين يكلف لا ستيفاء نجم قد حل لاحتمال الهلاك ثم اذا قبض الثمن يؤمر باحضاره لاستيفاء الدين لـقـيـامــه مـقـام الـعـيـن
ترجمہ اور انیسے ہی جبکہ راہن نے مرتبہن کو حکم کیا مرہون کے بیچنے کا پس مرتہن نے اس کو بیچ دیا اور شمن پر قبضہ نہیں کیا اس لئے کہ وہ دین ہوا ہے راہن کے حکم سے بیچنے کی وجہ سے پس ایسا ہو گیا گویا کہ راہن نے اس کو رہن رکھا ہے درانحالیکہ وہ دین ہے اور اگر مرتہن نے شمن پر قبضہ کر لیا تو شمن کو حاضر کرنے کا مکلف ہو گا بدل کے مبدل کا قائم مقام ہونے کی وجہ سے مگر جو شخص کہ شمن پر قبضہ کرنے کا متولی ہوگا وہ مرتہن ہو گا اس لئے کہ عاقد وہی ہے تو حقوق اسی کی جانب راجع ہوں گے اور مرتین جیسے مکلف ہو گا ر ہن کو حاضر کرنے کا پورے قرض کی وصولیابی کے لئے ایسے ہی مکلف ہو گا اس ایک قسط کو وصول کرنے کے لئے جس کا وقت آگیا ہے ہلاکت کے احتمال کی وجہ سے.
And likewise when the mortgagor orders the mortgagee to sell it, and he sells it but does not take possession of the price, because it becomes a debt by the sale with the mortgagor's order, so it is as if the mortgagor pledged it while it is a debt. And if he takes possession of it, he is required to produce it because the substitute stands in place of the original. However, the one who undertakes to collect the price is the mortgagee because he is the contractor, so rights revert to him. And just as he is required to produce the pledge to collect the entire debt, he is required to produce it to collect an installment that has become due, due to the possibility of loss. Then, when he collects the price, he is ordered to produce it for the collection of the debt because it stands in place of the specific item.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage deals with the scenario where the mortgagor orders the mortgagee (not a third-party 'adil) to sell the pledge. The ruling distinguishes two situations: (a) If the mortgagee sells but does not take possession of the price (thaman), the price becomes a debt (dain) owed by the buyer. In this case, the debt replaces the pledge (it is as if the debt itself is now the pledge). (b) If the mortgagee does take possession of the price (e.g., in a cash sale), then he must produce that price when demanding the debt from the mortgagor, because the substitute (badal) stands in place of the original (mubdal). The mortgagee, being the actual contracting party, is the one to receive the price. However, the mortgagee is required to produce the price even if the debt is payable in installments and only one installment has become due, because there is a risk (ihshtimal al-halak) of loss. The reasoning underscores that the price substitutes for the physical pledge, and the duty to produce it mirrors the duty to produce the original item.

Key Terms
بدل (badal): Substitute; here the price (thaman) replaces the pledged item as security.
مبدل (mubdal): The original; here the pledged property (marhun) which is replaced by the price.
نجم (najm): Installment of a debt that has become due.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling when the mortgagee sells the pledge with permission and takes possession of the price?
A) The mortgagee may keep the price and demand the debt separately.
B) The mortgagee must produce the price before demanding the debt.
C) The mortgagee must return the price to the buyer.
D) The mortgagee must wait until the full debt is due.

Key Takeaway
When a mortgagee takes possession of the sale price after selling the pledge with permission, he must produce that price before demanding the debt, because the price is the substitute for the pledge.

Production Duty for a Due Installment (Najm)
Ruling when mortgagee sells pledge by mortgagor's order: effect on production duty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the mortgagee must produce the price even for a single due installment of the debt, and identify the underlying principle of risk (ihtimal al-halak).

Core Idea
A single due installment triggers the production duty because of potential loss.

The previous lesson established that a mortgagee who takes possession of the sale price must produce it when demanding the debt. This lesson extends that rule to a specific situation: even if only one installment of a deferred debt has become due, the mortgagee must produce the price before collecting that installment. The reason given is 'li-ihtimal al-halak' (due to the possibility of loss). This shows the Hanafi concern for preserving the security until the debt is fully satisfied.

Guided Path
1
Recall the base ruling
Remember that the mortgagee must produce the price when demanding the full debt. This is the baseline.
From Lesson 1.
2
Identify the new scenario
Now consider a debt payable in installments. Only one installment (najm) has become due, not the whole debt. The mortgagee demands that installment.
Najm means a due installment.
3
Apply the extension
The text says he must produce the price even for that single installment. The reason is 'li-ihtimal al-halak' – because if the price is not produced, it could be lost, and the mortgagee's security would be diminished.
This is a precautionary principle.
4
Synthesize the principle
The duty to produce is not contingent on demanding the full debt; it is tied to any demand for payment that depletes the security. The substitute must be available until the debt is fully extinguished.

Ruling When the Trustee (Adil) Sells the Mortgaged Property on Order of the Pledgor
Ruling with proof: pledgee's obligation after trustee sells pawn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when the pledgor authorizes the trustee to sell the pawn and explain why the pledgee is not required to produce the pawn after the sale.

Core Idea
After the trustee sells the pawn, the pledgee can demand debt without producing the pawn.

In this lesson, we examine a specific scenario in the law of pawn (rahn): the pledgor authorizes a neutral third-party trustee (adil) to sell the pawned property. After the sale, the pledgee demands repayment of the debt. Is the pledgee required to first produce the pawn? The source text explains that the pledgee is not required, because the pawn has been converted into a debt and the pledgee no longer has power over the physical item. This ruling is based on the principle of takhliyah (vacating possession) and the avoidance of harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The pledgor (rahin) authorizes the trustee (adil) to sell the pawn (marhun). The trustee sells it for cash or credit. Then the pledgee (murtahin) demands his debt from the pledgor.
2
State the ruling
The pledgee is not compelled to produce the pawn before receiving payment. The sale is valid, and the pledgee's demand is rightful without prior production.
This is the core ruling.
3
Trace the legal reasoning
The duty of the pledgee is only takhliyah (vacating possession), not physical transfer. After sale, the pawn becomes a debt (dayn) in the hands of the buyer; the pledgee has no power over it. Requiring him to produce it would cause him harm without his consent.
The reasoning is based on inability and istihsan.
4
Note the distinction between fungible and non-fungible items
Before the sale, the requirement to produce the pawn depended on the nature of the pawn. For fungible (muhliki) items, the pledgee must produce because all places are equal for delivery. For non-fungible items, he is not required. After sale by the trustee, this distinction is irrelevant because the pawn is no longer in the pledgee's possession.
The distinction matters in the original scenario but is overridden by the trustee's sale.
5
Apply the ruling to similar cases
This ruling applies whenever the pawn is sold by a third party acting on behalf of the pledgor. The pledgee's inability to produce justifies the exception.
The reasoning can be extended by qiyas.

169 The book of pawn. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, volume 14. In the first case, the pledgee will be told to first produce the pawn and then collect his debt, because when the pawn is a fungible (muhliki) item, all places are equal for delivery. And this is why, by consensus, in the chapter of salam, it is not a condition to specify the place of delivery for such items. And if the item is of the second category, then the pledgee will collect his debt and the pledgee will not be burdened to produce the pawn in it itself, because the duty of the pledgee is delivery (takhliyah), whose reality is vacating; moving it is not necessary upon him, and also the pledgee would suffer harm from moving it when he did not commit to it. The pledgor said to the trustee to sell the pawn, so the pledgor's command is absolute, thus it includes both cash and credit. And if the pledgor authorizes the trustee to sell the pawn, and he sells it for cash or credit, it is permissible due to the absoluteness of the command. Then if the pledgee demands the debt, the pledgee is not compelled to produce the pawn because he has no power to produce it. Translation: And if the pledgor authorized the trustee to sell the pawn, then the trustee sold it for cash or credit, it is permissible due to the absoluteness of the command. Then if the pledgee demanded the debt, the pledgee is not compelled to produce the pawn because he has no power to produce it. Explanation: The trustee (adil) is the one with whom, by agreement of pledgor and pledgee, the pawn is kept. So if the pledgor told the trustee to sell the pawn, since the pledgor's command is absolute, it includes both cash and credit. Therefore, if the trustee sold it on credit, it is permissible. Nevertheless, during this, the pledgee demanded his debt from the pledgor, so his demand is rightful, but here the pledgee will not be ordered to first produce the pawn because the pledgee now has no power to produce the pawn, as is apparent.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is a ruling with proof, explaining the scenario where the pledgor (rahin) authorizes a third-party trustee (adil) to sell the mortgaged property (marhun). The passage begins by distinguishing two types of pawn: fungible (muhliki) and non-fungible. For fungible items, the pledgee (murtahin) must produce the pawn before claiming debt. For non-fungible items, the pledgee is not required to produce the pawn because his duty is only to vacate possession (takhliyah), not to physically transfer. The core ruling is: if the pledgor tells the adil to sell, and the adil sells for cash or credit, the sale is valid due to the absolute command. Then if the pledgee demands repayment of the debt, the pledgee is not compelled to produce the pawn because it has been sold and is no longer in his possession; the pawn has become a debt (dayn) in the hands of the buyer. The reasoning is istihsan based on inability and avoidance of harm. The analogy is drawn with salam contracts where specifying place is not required for fungibles.

Key Terms
عدل (adil): A trustworthy third party with whom the pawn is deposited by mutual agreement of pledgor and pledgee.
مرهون (marhun): The property that is pledged as security for a debt.
تخلیہ (takhliyah): Vacating possession; the act of delivering the pawn by removing oneself and leaving it accessible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The murtahin must first produce the marhun before claiming debt.
B) The murtahin can claim debt without producing the marhun because it has become a debt.
C) The sale is invalid because it was on credit.
D) The murtahin must wait until the adil collects the price.

Key Takeaway
After the adil sells the pawn, the pledgee is not required to produce it when demanding the debt because it is no longer in his possession.

6 min
Sale of Pawn by Pledgee with Permission
Explains the ruling when the pledgee sells the pawn with permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when the pledgee sells the pawn with the pledgor's permission and identify the conditions that determine the obligation to produce the price.

Core Idea
If the pledgee sells the pawn with permission, the substitute (price) stands in place of the pawn, but only if collected.

When the pledgor permits the pledgee to sell the pawn, the pawn transforms from a specific object into a debt owed by the buyer. The critical distinction is whether the pledgee has collected the price or not. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and legal consequences, including how the substitute (thaman) replaces the pawn (ayn) for the purpose of securing the debt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage distinguishes between (1) the pledgee sells but does not collect the price, and (2) the pledgee sells and collects the price. State each scenario clearly.
The ruling differs for each.
2
Understand the transformation
When the pawn is sold with permission, it becomes a debt (dayn) owed by the buyer. It is no longer a tangible 'ayn. This is because the sale is valid and the price is now owed.
The pawn is replaced by the right to the price.
3
Apply the principle of substitution
The Hanafi principle 'al-badal yaqumu maqam al-mubdal' (the substitute stands in place of the substituted) governs. The price (thaman) becomes the substitute for the pawn. If collected, it takes on the same legal role as the pawn.
If not collected, there is no substitute to produce.
4
Determine the obligation
If the pledgee has not collected the price, he is not required to produce the pawn when demanding his debt. If he has collected the price, he must produce the price because it now stands in place of the pawn.
This applies even if the debt is payable in installments.
5
Note the extension to installments
The obligation to produce the price exists for each due installment, not only for the full debt, due to the possibility of destruction of the pawn.
The logic is parallel to producing the pawn for each installment.

جو شخص کہ شمن پر قبضہ کرنے کا متولی ہوگا وہ مرتہن ہو گا اس لئے کہ عاقد وہی ہے تو حقوق اسی کی جانب راجع ہوں گے اور مرتین جیسے مکلف ہو گا ر ہن کو حاضر کرنے کا پورے قرض کی وصولیابی کے لئے ایسے ہی مکلف ہو گا اس ایک قسط کو وصول کرنے کے لئے جس کا وقت آگیا ہے ہلاکت کے احتمال کی وجہ سے پھر جب مرتہن نے شمن پر قبضہ کر لیا تو اس کو احضار ثمن کا حکم دیا جائے گا قرض کے وصول کرنے کے لئے شمن کے عین کے قائم مقام ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح اگر راہن نے مرتہن کو اجازت دیدی کہ وہ مرہون کو فروخت کر دے لہذا مرتہن نے اس کو فروخت کر دیا اور مرتہن نے ثمن وصول نہیں کیا تو بھی مطالبہ کے وقت مرتہن کو مرہون کو حاضر کرنے کا حکم نہیں دیا جائے گا اس لئے کہ اب رہن عین نہیں رہا بلکہ دین ہو گیا اور اس کا یہ دین ہونا اس بیع کی وجہ سے ہے جو راہن کے حکم سے ہوئی ہے بہر حال یہ عین اب دین ہو گیا اور یہ دین ہونا پہلے سے نہیں بلکہ اب ہوا ہے اور اگر یہ پہلے سے دین ہوتا اور اس کو عادل کے پاس رہن میں باتفاق طرفین رکھ دیا جاتا تو مرتہن کو مطالبہ دین کا حق ہوتا ایسے یہاں بھی ہے، ہاں اگر مرتہن نے شمن وصول کر لیا ہوتو چونکہ ثمن مرہون کے قائم مقام ہے اس وجہ سے اس کو احضار ثشمن کا حکم دیا جائیگا، اور ساتھ ہی ساتھ یہاں یہ بات ہونا بھی ضروری ہے کہ مشتری سے ثمن وصول کرنے کا استحقاق مرتہن کو ہے کیونکہ یہی مرتہن فروخت کرنے والا ہے اگر چہ یہ راہن کیجانب سے وکیل ہے تو بیع کے حقوق اس کی جانب راجع ہوں گے اور مجملہ حقوق کے مبیع کو سپرد کرنا اور شن وصول کرنا ہے۔ پھر واضح ہو کہ قرض قسط وار ہوتا ہے یکبارگی نہیں ہوتا لہذا ایسی صورت میں وہی حکم ہے جو پورا قرض وصول کرنے کی صورت میں یعنی قسط کو ادا کرنے کے وقت بھی احضار رہن کا بھی ایسے ہی حکم ہو گا جیسے پورا قرضہ ادا کرنے کے وقت احضار رہن کا حکم ہوتا ہے کیونکہ احتمال ہے کہ مرہون ہلاک ہو گیا ہو تو پھر یہ قسط اداء کرنا بھی لازم ہوگا۔ بہر حال جب مرتہن نے بحکم را بن مرہون کو فروخت کر دیا ہو تو اس کا شمن وصول کرنا مرتہن کا کام ہوگا پھر جب مرتہن نے ثمن وصول کر لیا تو اس کو اپنا قرض وصول کرنے کے لئے حکم دیا جائے گا کہ ثمن مذکور کو حاضر کرنے اس لئے کہ یہ ثمن عین مرہون کے قائم مقام ہے۔
What is the ruling if the pledgor gives permission to the pledgee to sell the pawn? And likewise, when the pledgor commands the pledgee to sell it, and he sells it and does not take possession of the price, because it becomes a debt due to the sale by the pledgor's command, so it becomes as if the pledgor pawned it while it is a debt. And if he takes possession of the price, he is compelled to produce it because the substitute stands in place of the substituted. However, the one who undertakes to take possession of the price is the pledgee because he is the contractor, so rights return to him. And just as he is compelled to produce the pawn for the collection of the entire debt, he is compelled to produce it for the collection of an installment that has become due, due to the possibility of destruction. Then when he takes possession of the price, he is ordered to produce it for the collection of the debt, because it stands in place of the 'ayn. Translation: And likewise, when the pledgor commanded the pledgee to sell the pawn, then the pledgee sold it and did not take possession of the price, because it became a debt due to the sale by the pledgor's command, so it became as if the pledgor pawned it while it is a debt. And if the pledgee took possession of the price, he is compelled to produce it because the substitute stands in place of the substituted. But the one who undertakes to take possession of the price is the pledgee because he is the contractor, so rights return to him. And just as he is compelled to produce the pawn for the collection of the entire debt, he is compelled to produce it for the collection of an installment that has become due, due to the possibility of destruction. Then when he takes possession of the price, he is ordered to produce it for the collection of the debt, because it stands in place of the 'ayn. Explanation: If the pledgor gave permission to the pledgee to sell the pawn, so the pledgee sold it and did not collect the price, then at the time of demand, the pledgee will not be ordered to produce the pawn because the pawn is no longer an 'ayn but has become a debt, and this becoming a debt is due to the sale that occurred by the pledgor's command. However, this 'ayn has become a debt now, not previously. And if it were a debt from before and it was placed with the adil as pawn by agreement of both parties, then the pledgee would have the right to demand the debt similarly here. Yes, if the pledgee collected the price, then since the price stands in place of the pawn, he will be ordered to produce the price. And along with this, it is also necessary that the right to collect the price from the buyer belongs to the pledgee, because he is the seller, even though he is an agent of the pledgor, so the rights of the sale revert to him, and the total rights are to deliver the sold item and to collect the price. Then it is clear that the debt is paid in installments, not all at once. So in this case, the same ruling applies as in the case of collecting the entire debt: at the time of paying an installment, the same ruling of producing the pawn applies as when paying the entire debt, because of the possibility that the pawn might be destroyed, so then paying this installment would also be necessary. Nevertheless, when the pledgee sells the pawn by the pledgor's command, his task is to collect the price. Then when the pledgee has collected the price, he will be ordered to produce it for collecting his own debt, because this price stands in place of the 'ayn.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, addressing the case where the pledgor (rahin) gives permission to the pledgee (murtahin) himself to sell the pawn. The ruling distinguishes two scenarios: (1) If the pledgee sells the pawn but does not collect the price, the pawn becomes a debt in the hands of the buyer, so the pledgee is not required to produce the pawn when demanding his debt. (2) If the pledgee does collect the price, then the price (thaman) stands in place of the pawn ('ayn), so the pledgee must produce the price when demanding debt. Additionally, the pledgee is the one entitled to collect the price from the buyer because he is the contracting party. The reasoning is based on the principle that the substitute (badal) takes the place of the substituted (mubdal). Also, if the debt is payable in installments, the obligation to produce the price exists for each due installment, because of the possibility that the pawn might be destroyed. This ruling also highlights that the pledgee acts as agent for the pledgor in the sale, but the rights of the sale (delivery of the sold item and collection of price) belong to the pledgee.

Key Terms
مرتهن (murtahin): The pledgee or creditor who receives the pawn as security for a debt.
ثمن (thaman): The price received from the sale of the pawn.
عین (ayn): The specific physical pawn itself, as opposed to a debt or substitute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the rahin permits the murtahin to sell the marhun, and the murtahin sells it and collects the price (thaman), is the murtahin required to produce the thaman when claiming his debt?
A) Yes, because the thaman stands in place of the 'ayn.
B) No, because the murtahin is the seller and owns the thaman.
C) No, because the thaman is now owned by the rahin.
D) Yes, only if the sale was for cash.

Key Takeaway
When the pledgee sells the pawn with permission, the price collected takes the legal place of the pawn and must be produced when claiming the debt.

Pawn Destroyed by Third Party: Diya as Substitute
Distinguishes the case of third-party killing from sale by pledgor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a third party kills a mortgaged slave and explain why the pledgor is not compelled to pay the debt until the pledgee collects the entire diya.

Core Idea
The diya substitutes the pawn; the pledgee must collect it fully before demanding the debt.

This passage from Al-Hidayah distinguishes two scenarios: when the pawn is sold by the pledgor's order and when it is destroyed by a third party. The ruling hinges on who caused the conversion of the pawn into a substitute. Understanding this distinction clarifies when the pledgee can demand immediate repayment versus when he must first collect compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage and note the contrast: (1) the pawn is sold by the pledgor's order, making the debt due; (2) the pawn is killed by a third party, making the diya a substitute.
The key word is 'bikhilaf' (unlike).
2
Analyze the cause of conversion
In the sale case, the pawn becomes a debt by the pledgor's own action (tasarruf). In the killing case, the pawn is destroyed by another's act, so the value becomes a substitute (khalaf) by court order.
The 'illa (cause) is the source of the conversion.
3
Apply the principle of khalaf
The diya is a substitute for the pawn; just as the entire 'ayn of the pawn must be produced, the entire substitute must be collected before the debt can be demanded.
Qiyas: the substitute stands in place of the original.
4
Derive the ruling
The pledgor is not compelled to pay the debt until the pledgee obtains the full diya from the 'aqila. The murtahin must wait up to three years if the diya is paid in installments.
This protects the pledgor from double liability.
5
Contrast with the sold pawn case
In the earlier case, the pawn became a debt by the pledgor's consent, so the murtahin could demand payment immediately without collecting the substitute.
The difference is based on who caused the conversion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رہن کے غلام کو کسی نے قتل کر دیا تو کیا حکم ہے وهذا بخلاف ما اذا قتل رجل العبد الرهن خطأ حتى قضى بالقيمة على عاقلته في ثلث سنين لم يجبر الراهن على قضاء الدين حتى يحضر كل القيمة لان القيمة خلف عن الرهن فلا بد من احضار كلها كما لا بدمن احضار كل عين الرهن وما صارت قيمة بفعله وفيما تقدم صار دينا بفعل الراهن فلهذا افترقا ترجمہ اور یہ حکم اس صورت کے خلاف ہے جبکہ کسی شخص نے رہن کے غلام کو خطام قتل کر دیا یہاں تک کہ اس کے خاندان پر قیمت کا فیصلہ کر دیا گیا تین سال میں تو راہن کو قرض ادا کرنے پر مجبور نہیں کیا جائیگا یہاں تک کہ مرتبین پوری قیمت حاصل کرے اس لئے کہ قیمت رہن کا خلیفہ ہے تو پوری قیمت کا احضار ضروری ہے جیسا کہ پورے عین رہن کا احضار ضروری ہے اور یہ قیمت نہیں بنتی ہے را ہن کے فعل سے اور پہلی صورت میں رہن دین ہوا تھا راہن کے فعل سے پس اسی وجہ سے یہ دونوں صورتیں جدا جدا ہو گئیں۔ تشریح اگر رہن کے غلام کو کسی نے نظام قتل کر دیا اور قاضی نے قاتل کے عاقلہ پر غلام کی قیمت واجب کر دی جس کو وہ قسط وار تین سال میں ادا کریں گے۔
What is the ruling if someone kills the mortgaged slave? And this is unlike the case when a man kills the mortgaged slave by mistake, such that the value (qima) is adjudged against his 'aqila (tribal kinsmen) to be paid in three years: the pledgor is not compelled to pay the debt until the pledgee collects the entire value, because the value is the successor (khalaf) of the pawn, so it is necessary to produce all of it, just as it is necessary to produce the entire 'ayn of the pawn. And this value does not become [a debt] by his (the pledgor's) action, whereas in the previous case, it became a debt by the pledgor's action. Therefore, these two cases differ. Translation: And this ruling is contrary to the case when a person kills the mortgaged slave by mistake, to the extent that the value is adjudged against his 'aqila to be paid in three years. The pledgor is not compelled to pay the debt until the pledgee obtains the entire value, because the value is the successor of the pawn, so it is necessary to produce all of it, just as it is necessary to produce the entire 'ayn of the pawn. And this value does not become [a debt] by the pledgor's action, whereas in the previous case, the pawn became a debt by the pledgor's action. Therefore, these two cases are distinguished. Explanation: If someone kills the mortgaged slave by mistake, and the judge makes the value (diya) obligatory upon the killer's 'aqila, which they will pay in installments over three years.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, contrasting the case where a third party kills the mortgaged slave with the previous cases where the pawn is sold by the pledgor's order. The key difference is the cause of the pawn's conversion: in the previous cases, the pawn became a debt (dayn) by the pledgor's own action (commanding sale), so the pledgee could demand debt without producing the pawn. Here, the pawn is destroyed by a third party, and the value (qima/diya) is awarded against the killer's 'aqila. This value is a substitute (khalaf) for the pawn, and it is not created by the pledgor's action. Therefore, the pledgor is not compelled to pay the debt until the pledgee actually collects the entire value from the 'aqila. The reasoning is based on the principle that the substitute must be produced in full, just as the physical pawn would have to be produced. The ruling distinguishes based on the source of the debt: one is by the pledgor's consent (sale), the other by a tort (killing). Thus, the pledgee must first obtain the diya before calling on the pledgor to pay.

Key Terms
قیمت (qima): The value or diya (blood money) assessed for the killed slave, paid by the 'aqila.
عاقلة (aqila): The tribal kinsmen or group responsible for paying diya on behalf of the killer in cases of accidental killing.
خلیفہ (khalifah): Successor or substitute; the value (qima) takes the place of the pawn ('ayn).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a third party accidentally kills a mortgaged slave (marhun) and the qadi awards diyah to be paid by the 'aqila in installments over three years, is the rahin compelled to pay the debt immediately?
A) Yes, because the slave is gone and the debt is due.
B) No, because the murtahin must first collect the full diyah which substitutes the pawn.
C) Yes, but only if the murtahin demands it.
D) No, because the rahin is not at fault.

Key Takeaway
When a pawn is destroyed by a third party, the diya becomes a substitute for the pawn, and the pledgee must collect it in full before demanding the debt from the pledgor.

Ruling When Murtahin Sells Pledge and Collects Price
Explaining the ruling on producing the price after sale of pledge with permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the murtahin's obligation to produce the price (thaman) after selling the pledged property with the raahin's permission, and distinguish the two scenarios based on whether the price was collected.

Core Idea
When the murtahin collects the price from the sale, he must produce it as a substitute for the pledge; otherwise, the pledge is converted to a debt.

After the murtahin sells the pledged property with the raahin's permission, his obligations change. This lesson, from the Sharh of al-Hidayah, clarifies that if the murtahin has collected the price, he must produce it when demanding the debt, because the price legally stands in the place of the original pledge. If he has not yet collected the price, the pledge is considered a debt and he cannot demand production.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Distinguish between (1) the murtahin selling the pledge with permission but not yet collecting the price, and (2) the murtahin selling and collecting the price.
The ruling changes based on whether the price has been collected.
2
Determine the legal nature in each scenario
When the price is not collected, the pledge becomes a debt (dayn) in the hands of the buyer. When collected, the price substitutes for the original pledge ('ayn).
The murtahin's right to demand production shifts from the original property to the price.
3
Understand the ratio (talil)
The price stands in place of the original pledge (al-thaman khalaf 'an al-ayn). This principle obligates the murtahin to produce the price when demanding repayment.
This talil is based on the idea that substitution preserves the pledge's function as security.
4
Apply to installment payments
Even when the debt is paid in installments, the murtahin must produce the corresponding portion of the price at each installment, because the price might be subject to loss.
Potential loss of the price triggers an obligation on the raahin to pay that installment again.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پھر جب مرتہن نے ثمن پر قبضہ کر لیا تو اس کو احضار ثمن کا حکم دیا جائے گا قرض کے وصول کرنے کے لئے ثمن کے عین کے قائم مقام ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح اگر راہن نے مرتہن کو اجازت دیدی کہ وہ مرہون کو فروخت کر دے لہذا مرتہن نے اس کو فروخت کر دیا اور مرتہن نے ثمن وصول نہیں کیا تو بھی مطالبہ کے وقت مرتہن کو مرہون کو حاضر کرنے کا حکم نہیں دیا جائے گا اس لئے کہ اب رہن عین نہیں رہا بلکہ دین ہو گیا اور اس کا یہ دین ہونا اس بیع کی وجہ سے ہے جو راہن کے حکم سے ہوئی ہے بہر حال یہ عین اب دین ہو گیا اور یہ دین ہونا پہلے سے نہیں بلکہ اب ہوا ہے اور اگر یہ پہلے سے دین ہوتا اور اس کو عادل کے پاس رہن میں باتفاق طرفین رکھ دیا جاتا تو مرتہن کو مطالبہ دین کا حق ہوتا ایسے یہاں بھی ہے، ہاں اگر مرتہن نے ثمن وصول کر لیا ہو تو چونکہ ثمن مرہون کے قائم مقام ہے اس وجہ سے اس کو احضار ثمن کا حکم دیا جائے گا، اور ساتھ ہی ساتھ یہاں یہ بات ہونا بھی ضروری ہے کہ مشتری سے ثمن وصول کرنے کا استحقاق مرتہن کو ہے کیونکہ یہی مرتہن فروخت کرنے والا ہے اگر چہ یہ راہن کی جانب سے وکیل ہے تو بیع کے حقوق اس کی جانب راجع ہوں گے اور مجملہ حقوق کے مبیع کو سپرد کرنا اور ثمن وصول کرنا ہے۔ پھر واضح ہو کہ قرض قسط وار ہوتا ہے یکبارگی نہیں ہوتا لہذا ایسی صورت میں وہی حکم ہے جو پورا قرض وصول کرنے کی صورت میں یعنی قسط کو ادا کرنے کے وقت بھی احضار رہن کا بھی ایسے ہی حکم ہو گا جیسے پورا قرضہ ادا کرنے کے وقت احضار رہن کا حکم ہوتا ہے کیونکہ احتمال ہے کہ مرہون ہلاک ہو گیا ہو تو پھر یہ قسط اداء کرنا بھی لازم ہوگا۔ بہر حال جب مرتہن نے بحکم راہن مرہون کو فروخت کر دیا ہو تو اس کا ثمن وصول کرنا مرتہن کا کام ہوگا پھر جب مرتہن نے ثمن وصول کر لیا تو اس کو اپنا قرض وصول کرنے کے لئے حکم دیا جائے گا کہ ثمن مذکور کو حاضر کرنے اس لئے کہ یہ ثمن عین مرہون کے قائم مقام ہے۔
Then when the murtahin took possession of the price, he will be ordered to produce the price for the purpose of collecting the debt, because the price stands in the place of the original property (ayn). Commentary: If the raahin gave permission to the murtahin to sell the pledge, so the murtahin sold it, but the murtahin did not collect the price, then at the time of demand, the murtahin will not be ordered to produce the pledge because now the pledge is no longer an 'ayn but has become a debt (dayn), and this becoming a debt is due to the sale that occurred by the raahin's command. In any case, this 'ayn has become a debt now, and this debt is not from before but has occurred now. And if it was a debt from before and was placed as a pledge with the adl by mutual agreement, then the murtahin would have the right to demand the debt. So it is here as well. Yes, if the murtahin collected the price, then since the price stands in place of the pledge, for this reason he will be ordered to produce the price. And along with this, it is also necessary here that the murtahin is entitled to collect the price from the buyer, because the murtahin is the seller, even though he is an agent on behalf of the raahin, so the rights of the sale revert to him, and the sum of rights includes handing over the sold item and collecting the price. Then it is clear that the debt is installment-based, not lump sum. Therefore, in such a case, the same rule applies as in the case of collecting the full debt, i.e., at the time of paying an installment, the ruling regarding producing the pledge will be similar to the ruling at the time of paying the full debt, because there is a possibility that the pledge may have been destroyed, so then paying this installment will also become necessary. In any case, when the murtahin sold the pledge by the command of the raahin, then collecting the price is the duty of the murtahin. Then when the murtahin collected the price, he will be ordered to produce the mentioned price for collecting his own debt, because this price stands in the place of the original property of the pledge.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage from the Sharh of al-Hidayah explains the ruling concerning the situation where the murtahin (pledgee) has sold the pledged property with the permission of the raahin (pledgor) and has collected the price (thaman). The key legal point is that once the murtahin collects the price, he is obligated to produce that price when demanding repayment of the debt from the raahin, because the price is legally treated as the substitute (khalaf) for the original pledged property ('ayn). The commentary distinguishes two scenarios: (1) If the murtahin sold but did not yet collect the price, then the pledge has been converted into a debt (dayn) by the raahin's permission, and the murtahin cannot be forced to produce the original pledge because it no longer exists as an 'ayn. (2) If he collected the price, then the price occupies the same legal status as the original pledge, so he must produce it. The ruling also applies to installment payments: at each installment due, the murtahin must produce the price corresponding to that installment, because there is a risk that the price might be lost, which would then obligate the raahin to pay that installment again. The commentary also notes that the murtahin has the right to collect the price from the buyer since he is the seller, even though he acts as agent for the raahin.

Key Terms
مرتہن (murtahin): The person who receives a pledge as security for a debt
راهن (raahin): The person who offers a pledge as security for a debt
ثمن (thaman): The price received from the sale of the pledged property
عین (ayn): The original physical property that was pledged
دین (dayn): A debt obligation that results from the sale of the pledge
قسط (qist): An installment payment of the debt

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When the murtahin sells the pledged property with the raahin's permission and collects the price, what is he required to do when demanding the debt?
A) Produce the original pledge
B) Produce the price
C) Nothing
D) Produce a different property

Key Takeaway
The price collected from the sale of a pledged property substitutes for the pledge, obligating the murtahin to produce it when demanding the debt.

Accidental Killing of Pledged Slave: Substitution Principle
Distinguishing the case where the pledge is destroyed by a third party's act from sale by raahin's permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a pledged slave is accidentally killed by a third party, explain why the murtahin must produce the full value before demanding the debt, and distinguish this case from sale by the raahin's permission.

Core Idea
The value is a substitute for the pledge; the party causing the conversion determines who must produce the substitute.

Last lesson we saw that if the raahin authorises the sale of the pledge, the murtahin need not produce it before demanding the debt. Now we encounter the opposite: the pledge is destroyed not by the raahin's act but by a third party's mistake. This lesson explores the critical distinction and the principle of substitution (khalaf) that governs the procedure.

Guided Path
1
Recall the previous case
Remember the situation from the previous lesson: the raahin allowed the murtahin to sell the pledge, converting it into a debt by his own act. The murtahin could then demand the debt without producing the pledge.
2
State the current case and ruling
Now a third party kills the pledged slave by mistake. The killer's 'aqila is ordered to pay the slave's value in installments over three years. In this case, the murtahin cannot force the raahin to repay the debt until he brings the full value.
The ruling is the opposite of the previous case.
3
Identify the legal cause (illa)
The difference lies in whose act caused the pledge to be converted into a substitute. In the previous case, the conversion was by the raahin's own permission (his act). Here, the conversion was by the killer's act, not the raahin's.
The 'illa is the origin of the conversion: raahin's act vs. third party's act.
4
Apply the principle 'al-qimat khalaf 'an al-rahn'
The value (qimah) is a substitute (khalaf) for the original pledge. Since the pledge was still in existence (substitute) but the conversion was not by the raahin, the murtahin must bring the substitute just as he would have to bring the original pledge. If the conversion were by the raahin's act, the murtahin need not bring the substitute because the raahin's action itself creates a debt.
This principle guides the procedural obligation.

Source Text

Arabic: This is contrary to the case when a man kills the pledged slave by mistake, to the extent that the value was assessed against his 'aqila in three years; the raahin is not compelled to pay the debt until the murtahin brings all of the value, because the value is a substitute for the pledge, so it is necessary to bring all of it, just as it is necessary to bring the entire physical pledge. And the value did not become such by his (the raahin's) act. In the previous case, it became a debt by the raahin's act; for this reason, they differ. Urdu: And this ruling is contrary to the case when a person killed the pledge slave by mistake, to the extent that the value was decreed against his family to be paid in three years. Then the raahin will not be compelled to pay the debt until the murtahin obtains the full value because the value is a substitute for the pledge. So producing the full value is necessary just as producing the full physical pledge is necessary. And this value does not become (a debt) by the raahin's act. In the first case, the pledge became a debt by the raahin's act; therefore these two cases are different. Commentary: If someone kills the pledge slave by mistake, and the judge makes the value obligatory on the killer's 'aqila to be paid in installments over three years, then here the murtahin cannot force the raahin to pay the debt until he brings the full value of the slave, because the value is a substitute for the pledge. So just as in the case of the pledge being present, producing the entire pledge is necessary, here producing the full value is necessary. And the difference is that here the pledge becoming a value/debt is not by the raahin's act, whereas in the first case, the pledge becoming a debt was by the raahin's act. For this reason, in the first case producing the pledge was not necessary, and here producing the pledge (i.e., its value) is necessary.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage contrasts two scenarios. In the previous case (lesson 1), the murtahin sold the pledge with the raahin's permission, converting it into a debt (dayn) by the raahin's own authorization; therefore, the murtahin was not required to produce the pledge before demanding the debt. In this new scenario, a third party kills the pledged slave by mistake, and the killer's 'aqila becomes liable to pay the value (qimah) in installments over three years. Here, the murtahin cannot demand the debt from the raahin until he has collected and can produce the full value of the slave. The reason is that the value is a substitute (khalaf) for the original pledge, and since the conversion to value occurred not by the raahin's act but by the killer's act, the murtahin must bring the value just as he would have to bring the original pledge if it were still extant. The Hanafi ruling emphasizes that the party whose action caused the conversion determines the procedural obligation: if the raahin's action caused the conversion (by authorizing sale), the murtahin need not produce the substitute; if an external act caused it, the murtahin must produce the substitute.

Key Terms
قیمت (qimah): The assessed value of the pledged slave that the killer's 'aqila must pay
عاقلہ (aqila): The paternal male relatives of the killer who are responsible for paying diyah in cases of accidental killing
خلف (khalaf): Substitute or replacement; here the value (qimah) is the khalaf of the original pledge

B) Collect the full value from the killer's 'aqila and produce it
C) Sue the killer
D) Return the slave's corpse

Key Takeaway
When a pledge is destroyed by a third party's act, the murtahin must produce the substitute (value) before demanding the debt, because the conversion was not by the raahin's act.

Murtahin Not Required to Produce Pledge When Placed with Adl
Ruling with ta'lil on murtahin's obligation to produce pledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a murtahin when the pledge is placed with an adl and then deposited elsewhere, and explain the reason (ta'lil) for this exception.

Core Idea
If the murtahin never possessed the pledge, he is not required to produce it.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in the law of pledge (rahn) where the murtahin (creditor) does not take actual possession of the pledged property. Instead, the raahin (debtor) places it with a trusted third party (adl) and allows that adl to deposit it with someone else. The passage clarifies that in such a case, the murtahin is not obligated to produce the pledge when demanding repayment of his debt, because he was never entrusted with its custody.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize the key elements: the raahin places the pledge with an adl, authorizes the adl to deposit it elsewhere, and the adl does so.
2
State the ruling
The murtahin is not required to produce the pledge when he comes to demand his debt.
This is an exception to the general rule that the murtahin must produce the pledge.
3
Locate the reason (ta'lil)
The passage gives the reason: 'because he was not entrusted with it (لم يؤتمن عليه) and its delivery is not within his power.'
The murtahin lacks control over the pledge.
4
Contrast with the general rule
In most other cases, the murtahin is ordered to produce the pledge because he has possession. Here, possession is absent.
Obligation to produce is tied to possession.
5
Understand the practical outcome
The murtahin can demand his debt directly from the raahin without first producing the pledge.
This protects the murtahin from impossibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage explains a case where the murtahin never takes actual possession of the pledge. Instead, the raahin places the pledge with a trusted third party (adl) and authorizes that adl to lodge it with another person. The adl does so. When the murtahin later demands his debt, he cannot be forced to produce the pledged property because he never had custody or control over it. This is an exception to the general rule that the murtahin must produce the pledge when demanding the debt. Ruling When the Adl Disappears After Depositing Pledge with His Dependent
Explaining that if the adl deposits the pledge with his dependent and disappears, the raahin is compelled to pay the debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for two disappearance scenarios and explain why the raahin is compelled to pay the debt.

Core Idea
No possession by the murtahin means no obligation to produce the pledge.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a practical issue in pledge (rahn) transactions: what happens if the trustee (adl) disappears with the pledged item or leaves it with his dependent? The murtahin (creditor) had no control over the pledge. The ruling clarifies that the raahin (debtor) must pay the debt directly, as the murtahin cannot be required to produce something he never possessed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
First: adl deposits pledge with his dependent and disappears. Second: adl disappears with the pledge itself. Note the common element: the adl is gone and the murtahin never had possession.
2
State the ruling for each
In both, the raahin is compelled to pay the debt. The ruling is the same.
3
Understand the talil (reason)
The reason given: producing the pledge is not upon the murtahin because he did not take possession of anything. Possession (qabd) is key.
This is a legal cause (illa) – lack of possession relieves the murtahin of the duty to produce.
4
Apply the principle to new variations
If the adl dies with the pledge, or the pledge is lost through the adl's negligence, similar reasoning applies: the murtahin is not liable.
The ruling protects the murtahin from loss he could not prevent.
5
Note the practical consequence
The raahin cannot avoid payment by claiming the pledge is unavailable. He must pay and then pursue the adl separately.
The raahin retains recourse against the adl for misappropriation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage presents two related scenarios. First: the adl deposits the pledged property with a person who is his dependent (e.g., a family member), and then the adl disappears. The holder of the pledge does not know to whom it belongs. The murtahin demands his debt. In this situation, the raahin is compelled to pay the debt because the murtahin never had possession of the pledge and cannot be required to produce something he never controlled. The underlying principle is that the obligation to produce the pledge rests only on someone who has actual possession or control over it. Since the murtahin never acquired possession (qabd), he is not required to produce the pledge, and the raahin must pay the debt directly.

Mortgagee's Duty to Produce Pawn When Deposited with Trustee
Ruling: mortgagee not compelled to produce pawn when deposited by trustee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a mortgagor deposits a pawn with a trustee authorized to further deposit it, and explain why the mortgagee is not required to produce the pawn when demanding the debt.

Core Idea
A mortgagee is not obliged to produce what he never possessed.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hanafi school on mortgage (rahn). When a mortgagor places the pawn with a trustee and grants him permission to deposit it elsewhere, the mortgagee’s right to demand repayment is not dependent on producing the pawn. Understanding the reasoning behind this exception clarifies the role of possession in mortgage transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Note the key elements: mortgagor (rahin), mortgagee (murtahin), trustee (adl), permission given to trustee to further deposit the pawn, and the trustee acts on that permission.
The trustee is a neutral third party, not the mortgagee's agent.
2
Recognize the General Rule
In standard cases, the mortgagee is required to produce the pawn when demanding repayment, because he has possession (qabd).
This is the default rule in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Identify the Exception
In this case, the mortgagee is not required to produce the pawn. The exception is triggered because the mortgagee never had possession, and the pawn was deposited by the mortgagor with a trustee who further deposited it with permission.
The exception is based on the mortgagee's lack of control.
4
Extract the ‘Illa (Reason)
The commentator explains: the mortgagee was not trusted with the pawn (lam yu'taman 'alayhi), so its production is beyond his power (lam yakun taslimuhu fi qudratihi).
The 'illa is the absence of possession and trust.
5
Apply the Ruling
Understand that this ruling is limited to cases where the mortgagee never had possession; if he had taken possession initially, he would be obliged to produce it.
This distinction is critical for correct application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
راہن نے مرہون کو عادل کے پاس رکھ دیا اس کو اپنے غیر کے پاس ودیعت رکھنے کی اجازت دیدی تو کیا حکم ہے؟
ولو وضع الرهن على يد العدل وامران يودعه غيره ففعل ثم جاء المرتهن يطلب دينه لا يكلف احضار الرهن لانه لم يؤتمن عليه حيث وضع على يد غيره فلم يكن تسليمه في قدرته
ترجمہ اور اگر راہن نے مرہون کو عادل کے پاس رکھا اور اس کو اجازت دیدی کہ وہ اپنے غیر کے پاس اس کو ودیعت رکھدے پس اس نے کیا پھر مرتہن نے اپنے قرض کا مطالبہ کرنے لگا تو اس کو رہن کے حاضر کرنے کا مکلف نہیں کیا جائے گا اس لئے کہ اس پر اعتماد نہیں کیا گیا اس حیثیت سے کہ راہن سے مرہون کو ) اس کے غیر کے پاس رکھا تو اس کو سپر د کر نا مرتہن کی قدرت میں نہیں ہے۔ تشریح پہلی صورتوں میں سے اکثر صورتیں وہ ہیں جن میں مرتین کو احضار رہن کا حکم دیا جاتا ہے لیکن اس صورت میں مرتہن کو احضار زہن کا حکم نہ ہوگا اور اس کے بغیر ہی وہ اپنے قرض کو طلب کرنے کا مختار ہوگا، صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ زید نے خالد سے قرض لیا خالد نے رہن رکھنے کا مطالبہ کیا مگر وہ رہن خالد کے پاس نہیں رکھا گیا بلکہ کسی عادل کے پاس رکھا گیا اور ساتھ ہی ساتھ راہن نے عادل کو یہ بھی اجازت دیدی کہ تم اس کو کسی اور کے پاس ودیعت رکھ سکتے ہو لہذا عادل نے اس کو کسی کے پاس رہن رکھ دیا تو خالد کو حق ہے کہ وہ زید سے اپنا قرض طلب کرے اور یہاں خالد کو احضار رہن کا حکم نہ ہوگا کیونکہ رہن کو حاضر کرنا خالد کے بس میں نہیں ہے۔
What is the ruling if the mortgagor placed the pawn with a trustee and gave him permission to deposit it with someone else, and he did so, then the mortgagee came demanding his debt? He is not compelled to produce the pawn because he was not trusted with it since it was placed with another, so its delivery was not in his power. Translation: If the mortgagor placed the pawn with the trustee and gave him permission to deposit it with someone else, and he did so, then the mortgagee began demanding his debt, he will not be compelled to produce the pawn because he was not trusted with it given that the pawn was placed with another, so its surrender is not in his power. Explanation: Most of the previous cases are those in which the mortgagee is ordered to produce the pawn, but in this case the mortgagee will not be ordered to produce it, and without that he is entitled to demand his debt.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hidayah, expanded by the commentator. The issue: when a mortgagor places a pawn with a trustee (adl) and authorizes the trustee to further deposit it with a third party, the mortgagee is not required to produce the pawn when demanding repayment. The reason ('illa) is that the mortgagee never had actual possession (qabd) of the pawn, nor was he entrusted with it — the trustee acted on the mortgagor's permission, not the mortgagee's. Therefore, the mortgagee cannot be held responsible for producing it. The mortgagee's right to demand the debt remains intact. This distinction is important: in other scenarios where the mortgagee had taken possession, he would be obliged to produce the pawn. Here, possession rests with the third party, relieving the mortgagee of that duty.

Key Terms
عادل (adl): A trustworthy third-party trustee who holds the pawn on behalf of both parties.
ودیعت (wadi'ah): Deposit; the act of leaving something in the custody of another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the trustee is the mortgagee's agent
B) Because the mortgagee never took possession and was not trusted with it
C) Because the pawn was destroyed
D) Because the mortgagee waived his right

Key Takeaway
The mortgagee is not required to produce the pawn when he never had possession, because the law does not demand the impossible.

Pawn Deposited with Trustee's Dependent Who Disappears
Ruling: mortgagor compelled to pay debt when trustee disappears with pawn deposited with dependent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a trustee deposits a pawn with his dependent and disappears, and explain why the mortgagor is compelled to pay the debt.

Core Idea
When the mortgagee never received possession, the pawn's loss falls on the mortgagor.

In a pawn (rahn) contract, possession by the mortgagee is typically required for the pawn to serve as security. But what if the trustee (adl) deposits the pawn with his own dependent and then disappears? The mortgagee demands his debt, but the pawn's whereabouts are unknown. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling and its underlying reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The trustee deposits the pawn with one of his dependents (e.g., family member) and then disappears. The mortgagee demands repayment of the debt from the mortgagor. The dependent holding the pawn does not know whose it is.
The key fact: the mortgagee never actually took possession of the pawn.
2
State the ruling
The mortgagor is compelled (yujbar) to pay the debt. He cannot demand the mortgagee to produce the pawn first.
The ruling is wajib: the mortgagor must pay.
3
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The mortgagee did not take possession of the pawn (lam yaqbid shay'an). Therefore, he has no duty to produce it. The pawn's loss is not his responsibility.
This is a talil (reasoning) based on the absence of possession.
4
Compare with similar case
The same ruling applies if the trustee disappears with the pawn itself and its location is unknown. In both cases, the mortgagee never had possession.
Consistency in the principle: liability rests on the mortgagor until delivery to mortgagee.
5
Note the practical implication
The mortgagor must pay the debt even though the pawn is not available. He can later seek recourse against the trustee for the lost pawn.
This prevents the mortgagee from being unfairly burdened.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عادل اپنے عیال کے پاس ودیعت رکھ کر غائب ہو گیا تو کیا حکم ہے
ولو وضعه العدل في يدمن فى عياله وغاب وطلب المرتهن دينه والذى فى يده يقول اودعنى فلان ولا ادرى لمن هو يجبر الراهن على قضاء الدين لان احضار الرهن ليس على المرتهن لانه لم يقبض شيئا وكذلك اذا غاب العدل بالرهن ولا يدرى اين هو لما قلنا
ترجمہ اور اگر رہن کو عادل نے اس کے پاس رکھ دیا جو اس کی عیال میں ہے اور عادل غائب ہو گیا اور مرتہن نے اپنا قرض طلب کیا اور وہ جس کے قبضہ میں رہن ہے کہتا ہے کہ فلاں نے میرے پاس اس کو ودیعت رکھا ہے اور مجھے معلوم نہیں کہ یہ کس کا ہے تو راہن کو قصاء دین پر مجبور کیا جائے گا اس لئے کہ رہن کو حاضر کرنا مرتہن کے ذمہ نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ اس نے کسی چیز پر قبضہ نہیں کیا اور ایسے جبکہ عادل غائب ہو گیا رہن کو لے کر اور نہیں جانی جاتی یہ بات کہ وہ کہاں ہے اسی دلیل کی وجہ سے جو کہ ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ تشریح عیال سے مراد وہ شخص ہے جو اس کی کفالت میں ہو اور اس کے نان نفقہ کا عادل ذمہ دار ہو (وسیأتی تفصیله)
What is the ruling if the trustee deposited the pawn with one of his dependents and disappeared, and the mortgagee demands his debt, and the one in whose hand it is says: 'So-and-so deposited it with me, and I don't know whose it is'? The mortgagor is compelled to pay the debt because producing the pawn is not upon the mortgagee since he did not take possession of anything. Likewise, if the trustee disappeared with the pawn and it is not known where it is, for the same reason we stated. Translation: If the trustee placed the pawn with one who is his dependent and the trustee disappeared, and the mortgagee demands his debt, and the one in possession says: 'So-and-so deposited it with me and I don't know whose it is,' then the mortgagor will be compelled to pay the debt because producing the pawn is not the mortgagee's responsibility since he did not take possession of anything. And similarly, when the trustee disappeared with the pawn and it is not known where it is, for the same reason we have stated. Explanation: By 'dependent' is meant the person who is under his guardianship and whose maintenance the trustee is responsible for.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage addresses a case where the trustee (adl) deposits the pawn with a dependent of his and then disappears. The mortgagee demands the debt from the mortgagor. The person holding the pawn does not know who it belongs to. The ruling: the mortgagor is compelled to pay the debt without the mortgagee needing to produce the pawn. The reasoning: the mortgagee never took actual possession (lam yaqbid shay'an), so he is not obligated to produce it. The loss of the pawn is not due to the mortgagee's negligence. This is consistent with the principle that if the pawn is destroyed or lost without fault of the mortgagee, the debt is considered satisfied (ista'fa al-dayn) and the mortgagee can demand payment. Here, the trustee's disappearance and the pawn's unknown location create a similar effect.

Key Terms
عیال (iyal): Dependents under the trustee's care, such as family members or servants.
قضاء دین (qada' al-dayn): Repayment of the debt; here it means the mortgagor is forced to pay.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the dependent refuses to deliver the pawn
B) Because the mortgagee never took possession of the pawn
C) Because the mortgagor authorized the deposit
D) Because the trustee is the mortgagor's agent

Key Takeaway
The mortgagee's lack of possession shifts the burden of producing the pawn to the mortgagor.

Denial of Pawn by the Holder: Loss Falls on Mortgagee
Ruling: mortgagee cannot claim debt from mortgagor until proving pawn status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when the pawn holder denies the pawn, and apply the rule that loss (tawa) falls on the mortgagee, thereby satisfying the debt.

Core Idea
Denial by the holder is treated as loss; the mortgagee bears it and the debt is deemed paid.

This passage deals with a scenario where the person entrusted with the pawn (the adl) denies it is a pawn and claims it as his own. The Hanafi ruling is that this denial is equivalent to the destruction of the pawn, so the loss falls on the mortgagee, and the debt is considered repaid. The mortgagee cannot recover the debt from the mortgagor unless he can prove the property was indeed a pawn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is the holder's denial of the pawn. The ruling: the mortgagee cannot demand the debt from the mortgagor until he proves the property is a pawn.
2
Locate the legal reasoning (talil)
The reasoning: the holder's denial causes the pawn to be considered lost (tawa), and loss of the pawn falls on the mortgagee by default, so the debt is deemed satisfied.
The analogy is to physical destruction, where the mortgagee also bears the loss.
3
Understand the analogy (qiyas)
The case of denial is compared to physical destruction: in both, the pawn is effectively lost, and the mortgagee bears the loss. This is a clear qiyas based on the common illah of loss.
4
Note the exception
If the mortgagee can produce evidence (claim and witnesses) that the property was indeed a pawn, he may still demand the debt from the mortgagor. Until then, the loss is final.
5
Practical consequence
The mortgagee must ensure proper documentation and witnesses when taking a pawn, especially if it is to be held by a third party.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جس کے پاس عادل نے ودیعت رکھی رہن سے انکار کر دے تو کیا حکم ہے؟
ولو ان الذى أودعه العدل جحد الرهن وقال هو مالى لم يرجع المرتهن على الراهن بشئى حتى يثبت كونه رهنا لانه لما جحد فقد توى المال والتوى على المرتهن فيتحقق استيفاء الدين فلا يملك المطالبة به
ترجمہ اور اگر وہ شخص جس کے پاس عادل نے ودیعت رکھی ہے رہن سے انکار کر دے اور کہے کہ یہ تو میرا مال ہے تو مرتہن را ہن سے کچھ نہیں لے گا یہاں تک کہ مرتین اسکار بہن ہونا ثابت کر دے اس لئے کہ مودع نے جب انکار کر دیا تو مال ضائع ہو گیا اور ہلاکت مرتبین پر پڑتی ہے تو قرض کی وصولیابی تحقیق ہوگئی تو مرتہن دین کے مطالبہ کا حقدار نہ ہوگا۔ تشریح ماقبل میں گذر چکا ہے کہ اگر مرہون ہلاک ہو جائے تو اسکی ہلاکت مرتبین پڑتی ہے اور ہلاکت رہن کی صورت میں مرتہن کو اپنے قرض وصول کرنے والا شمار کر لیا جاتا ہے لہذا اگر وہ شخص جس کے پاس عادل رہن کو رکھ کر غائب ہوا ہے رہن کا انکار کر کے یوں کہے کہ یہ تو میرا ذاتی مال ہے رہن نہیں ہے تو ید رہن کی ہلاکت کی صورت ہے جو مرتہن پر پڑے گی کیونکہ عادل کو یہ حق ہے کہ وہ رہن کو کسی کے پاس ودیعت رکھدے راہن اور مرتبہن کی اجازت سے ملتا ہے۔ لہذا صورت مذکورہ میں مرتہبن راہن سے اپنا قرض وصول نہیں کر سکتا بلکہ ہلاکت کی وجہ سے اس کو قرض کا وصول کرنے والا شمار کیا جائیگا ، البتہ اگر دعوئی اور گواہوں سے مرتہن اس کا رہن ہونا ثابت کر دے تو مرتہن کو دین کے مطالبہ کا حق ہو گا ورنہ نہیں۔
What is the ruling if the person with whom the trustee deposited the pawn denies it and says: 'This is my property'? The mortgagee will not get anything from the mortgagor until he proves that it is a pawn. Because when he denied, the property was lost and the loss falls on the mortgagee, so the debt is considered satisfied, and the mortgagee has no right to demand it. Translation: If the person with whom the trustee deposited the pawn denies it and says it is his own property, the mortgagee will not take anything from the mortgagor until he proves it to be a pawn. Because when the depositary denied, the property became lost and the loss falls on the mortgagee, so the debt is deemed recovered, and the mortgagee is not entitled to demand it. Explanation: It has passed before that if the pawn is destroyed, its destruction falls on the mortgagee, and in case of destruction, the mortgagee is considered to have recovered his debt. So if the person with whom the trustee deposited the pawn denies it and says it is his personal property, this is a case of loss falling on the mortgagee, because the trustee had the right to deposit it with someone, with the permission of mortgagor and mortgagee. Therefore, in this case, the mortgagee cannot recover his debt from the mortgagor; rather, due to the loss, he is considered to have recovered the debt. However, if the mortgagee proves through claim and witnesses that it is a pawn, then he will have the right to demand the debt; otherwise not.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage discusses the situation where the third-party holder of the pawn (the person with whom the trustee deposited it) denies that it is a pawn and claims it as his own. The ruling: the mortgagee cannot claim the debt from the mortgagor until he proves that the property is indeed a pawn. The reason is that the denial by the holder is tantamount to loss (tawa al-mal) of the pawn, and such loss falls on the mortgagee (at-tawa 'alal-murtahin). Once the pawn is lost, the debt is considered satisfied (istifa' al-dayn), and the mortgagee loses the right to demand repayment. This is similar to the case where the pawn is physically destroyed: the mortgagee bears the loss and the debt is deemed paid. However, if the mortgagee can prove (through evidence) that the property is a pawn, then he may still demand the debt from the mortgagor. The commentary emphasizes that this loss on the mortgagee applies because the trustee's deposit was authorized by both parties.

Key Terms
جحد (jahada): To deny; the holder's claim that the pawn is his own property.
توى (tawa): Loss or destruction of property; here, the pawn is considered lost due to denial.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the person holding the pawn denies it and claims it as his own, what must the mortgagee do before demanding the debt from the mortgagor?
A) Accept the loss and forfeit the debt
B) Prove that the property is a pawn
C) Sue the holder for theft
D) Wait for the trustee to return

Key Takeaway
Denial of pawn by the holder is treated as loss, and the mortgagee bears the loss, discharging the debt unless he proves it was a pawn.
