6 min
Duration of Mortgagee's Retention of Pawn
Ruling: mortgagee may keep pawn until debt is paid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule of permanent retention (habis da'im) in the contract of pawn (rahn) and explain why the mortgagee is not obliged to allow the sale of the pawn until the debt is fully paid.

Core Idea
The mortgagee has the right to keep the pawn until the debt is fully paid; this is the essence of the pawn contract.

This lesson examines a fundamental ruling in the Hanafi law of pawn (rahn): the mortgagee's right to retain the pawn until the debt is discharged. The passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar states clearly that the mortgagee is not obliged to allow the mortgagor to sell the pawn before repayment. Understanding this rule is crucial for grasping the security function of rahn and the rights of both parties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the legal act being described? The mortgagee retaining the pawn in his possession. What is the ruling? It is not obligatory for him to enable the mortgagor to sell it until the debt is paid.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does al-Quduri provide? He says 'because its rule is permanent retention until the debt is paid' (li'annahu hukmuhu al-habis al-da'im). This is a talil (rational reasoning) based on the definition of the contract.
The dalil is not a Quranic verse or hadith but a rational principle intrinsic to the contract.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this prove the ruling? The very purpose of pawn is to secure the debt; therefore, the mortgagee must have the right to hold the pawn until the debt is repaid. If the mortgagee were compelled to allow sale, the security would be lost.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there any disagreement among the schools? The passage indicates no dispute within Hanafi or across madhhabs; it is muttafaq alayh.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
This is the established position in the Hanafi school, recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah. The mufta bihi is that the mortgagee may retain the pawn until payment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مرتہن رہن کو کب تک اپنے پاس رکھ سکتا ہے؟
قال وان كان الرهن فى يده ليس عليه ان يمكنه من البيع حتى يقضيه الدين لان حكمه الحبس الدائم الى ان يقضى الدين على ما بيناه
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر رہن مرتہن کے قبضہ میں ہو تو مرتہن پر ضروری نہیں کہ وہ راہن کو مرہون فروخت کرنے کی قدرت دے یہاں تک کہ راہن اس کا قرض ادا کر دے اس لئے کہ رہن کا حکم حبس دائم ہی یہاں تک کہ راہن قرض ادا کر دے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم ( اوائل کتاب الرہن میں ) بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ تشریح جب تک مرتهن اپنا قرض وصول نہ کرے جب تک اس کو حق ہے کہ رہن واپس نہ کرے لہذا اگر راہن رہن کو فروخت کرنا چاہے تو مرتہن اسے فروخت کرنے نہ دے
How long can the mortgagee keep the pawn in his possession? He (al-Quduri) said: If the pawn is in his hand, it is not upon him to enable the mortgagor to sell it until the mortgagor pays the debt, because its rule is permanent retention until the debt is paid, according to what we explained. Translation: al-Quduri said: If the pawn is in the mortgagee's possession, it is not necessary for him to allow the mortgagor to sell it until the mortgagor repays the debt, because the ruling of the pawn is permanent retention until the debt is paid, according to the detail we explained earlier. Explanation: As long as the mortgagee has not recovered his debt, he has the right not to return the pawn. Therefore, if the mortgagor wants to sell the pawn, the mortgagee will not allow him to sell.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage states a fundamental principle of the contract of pawn (rahn): the mortgagee (murtahin) has the right to retain the pawn until the debt is fully repaid. This right is called 'habis da'im' (permanent retention). The mortgagee is not obliged to facilitate the sale of the pawn by the mortgagor before repayment. The commentary clarifies that the mortgagee may refuse to return the pawn even if the mortgagor wishes to sell it, because the pawn serves as security (wathiqa) for the debt. This retention continues until the debt is discharged. This ruling is well-established in the Hanafi school and is mentioned at the beginning of Kitab al-Rahn.

Key Terms
حبس دائم (habis da'im): Permanent retention; the mortgagee's right to keep the pawn until the debt is paid.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when can the mortgagee be compelled to allow the sale of the pawn?
A) At any time the mortgagor requests
B) Only after the debt is paid
C) When the pawn is perishable
D) When the mortgagee agrees

Key Takeaway
The mortgagee's right of permanent retention (habis da'im) is a fundamental rule of pawn: he may keep the pawn until the debt is fully paid, and is not compelled to allow its sale before then.

Rahn — Pledge
intermediate
8 min
Ruling when pledgor absconds after depositing pledge with a third party
Explains the ruling when the pledgor disappears after entrusting the pledge to a third party

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the pledgor's liability when the pledge is lost due to a third party's denial or disappearance, and apply the principle that loss falls on the pledgee where constructive possession exists.

Core Idea
If the pledgee never took possession, loss of the pledge does not relieve the pledgor of the debt.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses three scenarios where the pledgor has entrusted the pledge to a third party (the 'adil) and then either disappears or the third party denies the pledge. The Hanafi school carefully distinguishes between cases where the pledgee had possession and where he did not. The rulings prevent double recovery and ensure that the debt is properly accounted for.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios
The passage presents three sub-cases: (a) the depositary (where the adil left the pledge) disappears, (b) the adil himself disappears with the pledge, and (c) the depositary denies the pledge and claims it as his own. For each, note the status of the pledgee's possession.
2
Determine who bears the loss
For (a) and (b), the pledgee never had possession, so the loss does not fall on him; the pledgor must still pay. For (c), the depositary's denial is treated as destruction, and since the pledgee had constructive possession via the adil, the loss falls on the pledgee, satisfying the debt.
3
Examine the proof
The proof is based on the principle that the pledgee's right to demand production depends on possession. If no possession, no duty to produce. Also, denial is like destruction, and destruction counts as satisfaction.
4
Note the exception
If the pledgee proves through claim and witnesses that the property was indeed a pledge, he can demand the debt. This prevents collusion between the depositary and pledgor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عادل رہن کو ایسے شخص کے پاس ودیعت رکھ کر غائب ہو گیا جو اس کی عیال میں ہے، ادھر مرتہن نے اپنے قرض کا مطالبہ کیا اور عادل جس کے پاس مرہون کو رکھ کر گیا تھا کہ فلاں کی ودیعت تو میرے پاس ہے مگر مجھے یہ علم نہیں ہے کہ کس کی ہے تو راہن کو بدونِ احضار رہن قرض ادا کرنے پر مجبور کیا جائیگا کیونکہ مرتہن کے ذمہ نہیں ہے کہ وہ رہن کو حاضر کرے کیونکہ اسنے رہن پر قبضہ ہی نہیں کیا کہ اس کو احضار رہن کا حکم دیا جائے اور اسی طرح اگر عادل رہن لے کر غائب ہو جائے اور یہ معلوم نہ ہو سکے کہ وہ کہاں ہے تو بھی راہن کو قرض ادا کرنے پر مجبور کیا جائے گا اسی دلیل سابق کی وجہ سے۔
جس کے پاس عادل نے ودیعت رکھی رہن سے انکار کر دے تو کیا حکم ہے؟
ولو ان الذى أودعه العدل جحد الرهن وقال هو مالى لم يرجع المرتهن على الراهن بشئى حتى يثبت كونه رهنا لانه لما جحد فقد توى المال والتوى على المرتهن فيتحقق استيفاء الدين فلا يملك المطالبة به ترجمہ اور اگر وہ شخص جس کے پاس عادل نے ودیعت رکھی ہے رہن سے انکار کر دے اور کہے کہ یہ تو میرا مال ہے تو مرتہن را ہن سے کچھ نہیں لے گا یہاں تک کہ مرتین اسکار بہن ہونا ثابت کر دے اس لئے کہ مودع نے جب انکار کر دیا تو مال ضائع ہو گیا اور ہلاکت مرتبین پر پڑتی ہے تو قرض کی وصولیابی تحقیق ہوگئی تو مرتہن دین کے مطالبہ کا حقدار نہ ہوگا۔ تشریح ماقبل میں گذر چکا ہے کہ اگر مرہون ہلاک ہو جائے تو اسکی ہلاکت مرتبین پڑتی ہے اور ہلاکت رہن کی صورت میں مرتہن کو اپنے قرض وصول کرنے والا شمار کر لیا جاتا ہے لہذا اگر وہ شخص جس کے پاس عادل رہن کو رکھ کر غائب ہوا ہے رہن کا انکار کر کے یوں کہے کہ یہ تو میرا ذاتی مال ہے رہن نہیں ہے تو ید رہن کی ہلاکت کی صورت ہے جو مرتہن پر پڑے گی کیونکہ عادل کو یہ حق ہے کہ وہ رہن کو کسی کے پاس ودیعت رکھدے راہن اور مرتبہن کی اجازت سے ملتا ہے۔ لہذا صورت مذکورہ میں مرتہبن راہن سے اپنا قرض وصول نہیں کر سکتا بلکہ ہلاکت کی وجہ سے اس کو قرض کا وصول کرنے والا شمار کیا جائیگا ، البتہ اگر دعوئی اور گواہوں سے مرتہن اس کا رہن ہونا ثابت کر دے تو مرتہن کو دین کے مطالبہ کا حق ہو گا ورنہ نہیں۔
A trustworthy person deposited the pledge with someone who is of his household and disappeared, then the pledgee demanded his debt, and the trustworthy person with whom the pledge was deposited said: 'So-and-so's deposit is with me, but I do not know whose it is.' Then the pledgor will be forced to pay the debt without producing the pledge, because it is not the pledgee's responsibility to produce the pledge, as he did not take possession of it such that he could be ordered to produce it. Similarly, if the trustworthy person takes the pledge and disappears, and it cannot be known where he is, the pledgor will also be forced to pay the debt for the same reason as before.
What is the ruling if the one with whom the trustworthy person deposited the pledge denies it?
"And if the one with whom the trustworthy person deposited the pledge denies the pledge and says 'It is my property,' the pledgee cannot recourse to the pledgor for anything until he proves that it is a pledge. Because when he denied, the property has perished, and the loss falls on the pledgee, so the satisfaction of the debt is realized, and he does not have the right to demand it." Translation: And if the person with whom the trustworthy person deposited the pledge denies the pledge and says 'It is my property,' then the pledgee will not take anything from the pledgor until he proves that it is a pledge. Because when the depositary denied, the property became lost and its destruction falls on the pledgee, so the recovery of the debt is realized, and the pledgee is not entitled to demand the debt. Explanation: It has passed before that if the pledge perishes, its destruction falls on the pledgee, and in case of destruction of the pledge, the pledgee is considered to have collected his debt. Therefore, if the person with whom the trustworthy person deposited the pledge denies it and says 'It is my personal property, not a pledge,' then this is a case of destruction of the pledge that falls on the pledgee, because the trustworthy person has the right to deposit the pledge with someone, by permission of the pledgor and pledgee. So in this mentioned case, the pledgee cannot collect his debt from the pledgor; rather, due to the destruction, he will be considered as having collected his debt. However, if the pledgee proves through claim and witnesses that it is a pledge, then he has the right to demand the debt; otherwise not.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof addressing scenarios where the pledgor absconds after entrusting the pledge to a third party (the 'trustworthy person' or 'adil). The passage presents three sub-cases and their rulings. First: If the trustworthy person deposits the pledge with someone else and disappears, or if the trustworthy person himself disappears with the pledge, the pledgor is forced to pay the debt without producing the pledge. This is because the pledgee never took possession, so he cannot be ordered to produce it; the debt remains due. The proof is the previous reasoning that the pledgee's right to retain is based on possession. Second: If the depositary denies the pledge and claims it as his own, the pledgee cannot demand the debt from the pledgor until he proves the pledge. Because the denial amounts to destruction (tawiya) of the pledge, and that destruction falls on the pledgee, counting as satisfaction of the debt. Third: If the pledgee proves through evidence that the property is indeed a pledge, then he may demand the debt. The passage emphasizes that the pledgee's loss is considered as recovery of the debt, preventing double recovery.

Key Terms
عادل (adil): The trustworthy person who mediates between pledgor and pledgee; he holds the pledge but is not the pledgee.
مرتهن (murtahin): The pledgee, i.e., the creditor who holds the pledge as security.
رهن (rahn): The pledge or collateral given as security for a debt.
ودیعت (wadi'ah): Deposit; the act of entrusting property to another for safekeeping.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the person with whom the trustworthy person deposited the pledge denies it and claims it as his own, what happens to the debt?
A) The pledgee can still demand the debt from the pledgor.
B) The pledgee cannot demand the debt until he proves the pledge.
C) The pledgor is freed from the debt immediately.
D) The trustworthy person must pay the debt.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, loss of the pledge due to a third party's denial or disappearance is treated as satisfaction of the debt unless the pledgee can prove the pledge.
